<Author>Barb5454
<Content>Mutton sold as Lamb We just came back from the Riu Taino in Punta Cana. We usually go Mexico through Signature Vacations but decided to try something different this year.The Riu Taino is described by the Riu Group as a 5* hotel, and by Sunquest (our tour operator) as a 4* hotel. It is at best, with a generous evaluator, a 3*.We had booked a family suite and a hotel room. When we arrived (late in the evening), we were given 2 room keys. I asked the front desk clerk which was the family suite and which was the hotel room. He was confused by this, and ended up telling me that they were both family suites - the hotel had given us more than we had paid for and would lose money on us.We were led through the grounds to the 2 rooms, both of which appeared to be what are described by Sunquest as Supersaver rooms, that is, very small rooms.We returned to the front desk in the dark through the maze that is the layout here to ask for the suite we had paid for. We were told that it was our fault, because we had asked that the family suite and the hotel room be close or adjoining, and those were the 2 closest rooms they had. The fact that we had paid several hundred dollars more for the family suite did not seem to matter to them.We were then given a family suite (which was a good size) a short distance from the hotel room where our daughter's friend stayed. There is no way anyone could describe the suite as 4 or 5 star accomodation. There was an air conditioning unit in the main room that looked like it belonged on a scrap heap - it was rusted and pitted, and, needless to stay, did not work well.We were provided with 1 towel in this unit that sleeps 4. No hand towels or face cloths. There was a spill on the floor that had not been cleaned. The clock did not work. The furniture was old - the dresser drawers could not slide in  out because the runners were gone.On 2 occasions, we asked for a clock that works, without success. When I called the second time to make the request, I was asked by the front desk clerk why I wanted a clock. I said I wanted to know the time. He said It's 7:20. And I never got the clock.The fitness centre is a joke. The equipment is antiquated. I have never seen a treadmill, even the cheapest one, that does not incline, but the treadmill(s) here did not. I ask the attendant if he could turn the TV on while I exercised. The TV did not of course work. There were wires hanging down that looked like they had been there forever.One of the reasons we chose the Riu Taino was for the watersports, in particular, sailing. If you want to sail, do not come to this hotel. They have contracted out the watersports to ScubaCaribe. ScubaCaribe is interested in the watersports that it can sell to you, such as parasailing. They have no interest in the free watersports. When we first enquired about taking out a sailboat, we were told that they had 5 Hobie Cats, 3 of which were broken, leaving 2 sailboats for 3 or more Riu resorts (the Taino alone has 620 rooms). When we finally managed to get a sailboat (only once in the week we were there), we had to wait 10 - 15 minutes (from the 1 hour we had the boat) for one of the ScubaCaribe people to saunter down to the water and assist us in getting the boat out.The tennis courts were interesting. Sand on top of concrete. Made for interesting bounces.There were some positives. The food is (barely) alright. The setting is lovely, as is the beach. The waitstaff were great.My sense of this place was that it was once really nice. There are annual tourist award plaques on the wall in the reception area, ending in 2004. It looks like that's when the Riu Group decided to use its capital budget for the swankier hotels down the beach, in particular, the Riu Palace Punta Cana. That's fine but it should not describe this hotel as 5* and Sunquest should not be selling this mutton dressed up as lamb.Lessons learned: I will never use Sunquest again. I will never stay at a Riu resort again.  
<Date>Jan 4, 2009

<Author>PegToronto_Canada
<Content>Excellent service! Spent the first week of December 2008 at the Riu Taino in Punta Cana. This was our first visit to Punta Cana, and our first vacation with our son who is 18 months old. The service was outstanding! From the moment we checked in, which was very late at night 11ish, and with a baby wired for sound (very hyper), all we wanted was to get to our room and have a quick bite to eat. The check in was amazingly fast, no paperwork to be signed, everything ready to go, with a late night snack waiting for us at one of the bars. Everyday after, I can honestly say that we were treated like gold. Our initial room was a little on the small side and when we inquired if there were any larger rooms available we were instantly moved into a family suite, facing the ocean at no additional cost to us. Riu staff ensured that we had everything that we needed, extra pillows, a crib for Jules and lots of drinkable water. That same service happened at the main buffet restaurant as well. First night we sat in a section, got to know the waiter and the next night the same table was reserved for us, with a high chair and a glass of red wine waiting for me. Loved the service...best I have experienced in all of the Caribbean. Jules was a hit with everyone there too. Dominicans love babies and make sure that the babies are well taken care of. I gave this hotel a 3 star rating because the actual resort is starting to seriously show its age. A lot of the furniture has tears/rips in the material, and the buildings are somewhat run down. We have stayed in Mexico on numerous occasions, (Puerto Vallarta, Cancun and Cozumel) and the Riu Taino is not a 4 star to me based on what we have experienced in Mexico. With this being our first visit to the Dominican, I am not sure if my expectations were too high, but thought I should share my thoughts. The beds were exceptionally hard...and I like hard beds, so for me to complain is rare! They also did not have room service...a pet peeve and one that would not normally affect me except that to get a cup of coffee first thing in the morning I had to walk from one side of the resort to the other...which on the first couple of days was fine...nice walk, great weather...but by day 4 I really would have liked to have my coffee waiting for me! Call me spoiled, but when I am on vacation I do like an occasional breakfast in bed! Beach was the best of all the properties on that strip. Lovely white sand, with a constant gentle breeze and lots of well established palm trees for cover if you wanted it. Food was fine, no complaints. Lots of choices and plenty of fruit. Did not like the specialty restaurants though, buffet turned out to be better. Not much to do unless you take one of the excursions (you are looking at a cost of 80 - 100 US Dollars per person) and then with us having a baby we were really limited. Again, very different from Mexico where you can leave the resort and head into town and experience all kinds of things for free. Overall I would highly recommend this hotel for anyone who does not care if they have room service, do not mind the smell of mold and things not looking brand new. If this review were only about the service I would give it a 5, as I can honestly say that this was the best service we have ever received.  
<Date>Dec 23, 2008

<Author>mom1991
<Content>Family Bonding! What an experience! Sun, white sand and family! Punta Cana is fabulous! What would I recommend to others?... This resort is good for teens/adults (ours are 12, 15 and 17) but there wasn't anything for younger kids to do. You can buy blow-up pool toys there but they are pricey - we brought our own - (you can leave them behind). Plan on doing some excursions (we HIGHLY recommend the dune buggy experience with swimming in an underground natural pool!) BUT wait till day 3 to go. You need at least that much time to get into the swing of things, get your body used to the food, the laid-back pace and to start on your tan! Don't bother bringing your blow dryer - they have them in the bathrooms. If you really need to plug something in, the front desk rents plug adapters for $1 US for your stay. The nightly entertainment was totally lame so be prepared to be creative with your evenings with the kids. DO take advantage of the bricked sidewalk that runs along the beach from one end of the Riu properties to the other end. DO take advantage of the pools/eatery's offered at the other Riu resorts you can play at. The a la cartes were nothing special - just the same buffet choices in a different location. If you are a vegetarian - learn how to ask is there meat in this? in Spanish - most everything does have meat. DO take the Spanish classes offered. DO take your free scuba lesson in the pool. DO play water polo (it's a hoot!). If you can, DO stay for 10 days. One week was definately not enough and 2 weeks would have been too much. 10 days would have been perfect. And please, DO set your alarm for 5:30 am the morning you are leaving. Get up and walk down to the beach chairs, settle in and watch the sun rise. The only sound is the waves crashing and you can see at least a trillion stars (including the big dipper - which is upside down). These peaceful moments, with my family, was the perfect way to end the trip.

<Author>SimonUA
<Content>Great Place on a Budget My fiancee and I spent five nights at the Riu Taino in late August. We were traveling on a budget and the idea of an all-inclusive resort in a country we were not familiar with - our Spanish is also very basic - was appealing to us. The overall cost/performance ratio was excellent, which is also why I rate the hotel Excellent as I am considering what we got for what we paid. Otherwise, I would probably rate it Above Average.The staff was extremely friendly. Many spoke at least some English, and we were able to communicate with others in basic Spanish. Every time we asked for help, whether it'd be information at the reception or getting a table under a fan (keep that one in mind), someone was quickly and friendly helping us. Our rooms were always cleaned very well even to the point where some of the less obvious items, such as sand on the tile floor, was swept up. The towel animals and figures decorated with flowers were also very lovely and entertaining. The staff in my opinion deserves an excellent rating; I don't know what they could have done better.The accommodations and the grounds were well kept. As far as I remember I did not see any damaged objects, buildings with peeling paint, etc. The rooms were spacious and included two beds and a table as well as a ceiling fan and air conditioning, which we took advantage of as the humidity was extreme. The balcony had a great view onto the luscious greenery, and the bathroom and walk-in closet with refrigerator while small were adequate in size.The food was very good and offered a wonderful variety of seafood, meats, salads, sides, etc. The Riu Taino also has three specialty restaurants which you need to reserve seats to in the reception area (there is a desk in the mornings); however, the buffet was no step behind. If you desire a more intimate and romantic setting, go to the restaurant, but definitely try the food at the buffet as well - you won't regret it. The snack bars and drink bars were also very good and had variety. You're in an all-inclusive, so you won't find top-shelf liquor. I would probably recommend the beer as well as some lighter mixed drinks as the Dominicans seem to think the more liquor the better in a drink. We found that they were overpowering to the point where they were not drinkable at times, so be sure to let your bartender know your preference.I worked out once in the gym on Caribbean Street - the street that's part of the Riu resorts and in between the Taino and the Macao. This was a very dated gym and equipment sets were incomplete. This is definitely an area for improvement, so don't expect much there; however, it's still good enough to work out if you want it to be.The resort has two pools, and you should definitely try the swim-up bart - it's something else to sit on a stool in the pool while sipping a drink made fresh for you right there. =)The beach is gorgeous - very fine sand. The palms are wonderful, and you can spend hours dozing on a sun chair while the breeze keeps you cool and insect bite-free. You should not have to worry about stepping on anything sharp in the water; however, do pay attention to swimming in the two sectioned off areas as motorized equipment as not allowed there. The boats get pretty close to the shore, so be careful where you dive or snorkel.Last but not least, even though you are in an all-inclusive and tips are said to be included, please tip your bartender , your chambermaid, your server. or anyone else, whom you appreciate. We took a good amount of $1 bills with us - they go a long way there. Overall, we enjoyed our visit tremendously and certainly recommend it to anyone, especially when traveling on a budget.

<Date>Jul 20, 2008
<Rating>5	5	4	5	5	5	5	3	

<Author>maboscel
<Content>Would go back in a heartbeat We had such a great time. First thing - I asked for a room near the beach - and while none were available when we arrived, the next morning we were given a 2nd story room as close to the beach as you can get! It was superb! We are not your typical vacationers, I think, in that we enjoy doing things - being active - and using the ocean rather than a pool. We also are picky eaters in that we like to eat healthy food. We were not disappointed. While the menu does not vary much at the buffet, there is always plenty to choose from. Each night they had more than one fish entre, plus chicken, pork, ham, etc. along with fruit, vegetables, fresh breads, desserts, etc. Breakfast they had just about anything you can imagine - except oatmeal - and the fruit smoothies were the best!! But the buffet closes at 10am - then only a marginal continental b'fast until 1pm - so don't miss the buffet or you go hungry....... The waiters were exceptional. We ate at the Italian restaurant - a really nice change of pace - and also there was a night with dancing and special Caribbean food - and that too, was a nice change of pace. You can also walk over to the Riu Bamboo at any meal and eat there. Their buffets were larger, offered a different variety of food and I'd suggest going over there at least once. Watersports - not touched on much in these forums - so I will since we used daily. There are watersports buildings with 2-3 catamarins, sailboat, numerous windsurfers and kayaks about every 200 feet or less. You go there and sign up for an hour usage. Best to go the day before you want to use a catamarin as it fills up as the day goes on. But you can sign up every day for a week all at once if you want to - or go one hour one place and walk down the beach and sign up for an hour at the next place. The catamarins are in demand, but the other equipment is not, so the hour rule isn't enforced I don't think. Punta Cana doesn't have strong winds like the north coast and the beach is such that it's only shallow a short ways out and then deepens quickly. Thus, it makes it hard to learn to windsurf or to even get started. Noone ever planed there. We had a blast with the catamarins. Had never sailed one before, but they are easy to do and quite safe. There are reefs galore out there, however, so you have to watch scraping the boat. We actually surfed waves with them. It was fun. The equipment is in decent shape - some of the windsurf boards have missing footstraps and such, and there were no harnesses. The snorkelling was just ok. The Taino has a grassy reef enclosed in their swimming area, and fish will flock to you looking for food (I brought out bread and mashed bananas in a baggie to feed them the 2nd time.) But, the reef is pretty much dead so if you go anywhere else, there's no fish, no life to speak of. We also snorkelled WAY out near the wreck offshore (had to watch out for boats speeding by..... and that was neat - got to only about 40 feet of water and clear as a bell. Nice reef formations, but its pretty dead. Worth doing tho. Ok - the rooms were...... decent. Never had trouble with power, airconditioning or hot water. There ARE two beds tho - one double bed and one twin. We had no problem sleeping on the double, but for some people, it might present a problem. We preferred Taino over Bamboo in that the rooms of the Bamboo were quite a distance walk from the beach as opposed to our room - a few steps. Otherwise, the Bamboo has several advantages in that the nightly entertainment facility is an open air one - so the smokers don't bother you like they do at Taino's facility which is a closed room; the buffets are larger and have more variety - plus they greet you with a Tequila Sunrise upon entry at dinner; and the lobby area is gorgeous. But, the vendors were there more frequently than at Taino. Oh, vendors are not a problem at the beach. They may walk by, but don't stop to bug you. Only stop if you ask. We didn't see much of the nightly entertainment - for one, it was smoky in there, and for another, the talent is mainly locals - and while they CAN dance, once you see them, it's basically the same thing in different costumes. The Michael Jackson show tho was superb. We only caught the tail end and wished we'd seen it all. Regarding tipping - these employees make about $50US a week and work 10-12 hrs a day and do a super job. We ended up tipping many of the waiters and waitresses a $1 here and there - and once gave a guy $5 - then realized that's half his wages for one day! not a big deal to us, but a BIG deal to the Dominicans. So, don't be stingy, We didn't know it, but you can change your large US bills for $1 bills at the front desk. They are happy to do that for you, as they know where they are going.... Taxi from the airport cost us about $33 with tip; gas is close to $6/gallon there. We also took the public bus to Santo Domingo and then another one up to Cabarete. Email me if you have any Q's. We also loved the dancing they had at night - a pool and beach party; aerobics in the sand in the morning; Merengue lesson in the afternoon. We did not go to the Island Sanoa. It is a two hour bus ride each way - and didn't want to spend our vacation time on a bus. Hear you can take a catamarin tho. Now - That might be a great way to go!

<Content>Great Time at Riu Taino My girlfriend and I stayed at the Riu Taino from May 24-29th, 2008. We had a great time, and would certainly go back to the Taino. The activities put on by the Animacion staff were fun to watch. Room:Our room was perfectly fine. Maybe a little older, but still perfectly clean, and the AC and everything worked fine, no problems. We even had a nice little private porch, which was nice to sit and have a drink on. The maid did a great job keeping the room clean, and the mini bar was always replenished. Food:The breakfast buffet in the main dining room was always fine. We typically stuck to the fresh fruit and muffins, which were fine. The INDOOR lunch buffet in the main dining room was fine as well, but the OUTDOOR lunch buffets were a bit more interesting. There seemed to always be some bugs, flies and birds swarming around the outdoor lunch buffets, and didn't seem to be too sanitary. The dinners were great. The dinner buffet in the main dining room was fine as well, but we much preferred the specialty restaurants. For some reason due to either scheduling or being late on making the dinner reservations, we only ending up eating at the Italian restaurant and one other specialty restaurant (Mexican night), and we didn't get a chance to eat at the Steak House. However, both were good, but we enjoyed the Italian restaurant so much we ended up eating there 3 nights in a row (Gustavo and Johanna are a great waitstaff). Other:The little shops on Caribbean Street were fun to browse through, and all locals we met seemed very friendly. If you have any other questions feel free to contact me, I'd be happy to elaborate on any aspect of my trip. It was a great time, and we would certainly go back in a heartbeat. I miss the beach already!

We arrived at 4 a.m. Check in took all of five minutes and within another five minutes of arrving in our room, our baggage was delivered. We were very pleased with the room. This hotel is older and not as fancy as the Macao and the Palace but it is absolutely fine! It was just as good as our hotel in Paris last summer. We found the quality of the housekeeping to be excellent. I agree, however, with other reviews about the sheets being a little small and there were no mattress covers so each morning, the bed was quite a mess. I found the beds comfortable and, yes, the pillows were small but in the scheme of things, that is not an issue. the only issue we had with the room was regarding the air conditioning which did not work one day (we had left a window open and it will not work until it is closed) and within 5 minutes of calling, someone arrived. We were impressed!We had some built in concern about the buffet, based on reviews we had read, however, we were most impressed. Yes, you see much the same thing each day, but there is so much variety that it is impossible to get bored.Staff was friendly and attentive. We spent most of our time by the pool. It is incredibly close to the beach so we would move back and forth. Yes, you need to get down quickly in the morning to reserve you chair, but we found we wanted to be down there early anyway. That is when it is most quiet. By mid-morning, the beach gets quite congested and we enjoyed the peacefulness the early morning provided. There was always lots of activity around the pool and although we were rather lazy, we enjoyed watching the water fitness, dance classes, etc.It was a great holiday. There seems to be a great deal of disagreement on this resort. I think there are newer and older rooms. If you get a room in the newer sector, it seems to be fine. We talked to another couple who were not pleased, and they were moved immediately. They were pleased with the reception they received to their request.I would not hesitate to recommend this hotel. If you are looking for fancy, you might want to look beyond the TAino, we were very happy with our experience.

<Author>davedr
<Content>Second Trip to Punta Cana -Riu Taino not the best!!! Enjoyed our stay at the Riu Taino Feb 20-27th (Two adults age 41 and 37, two kids 14 and 12, Mom and Dad in-law 77 and 79 years)but were disappointed with a few things. They are firm beds, and yes smaller than what you may be used to....but just have a rum before bed!! Ha ha. We asked the front desk for blankets and they delivered them before 3 that day, then all was well. The water and beer guy was good the first two days then we didn't see him much. Maybe should have tipped more????Hotel staff at the restaurants, bar, pool all great. Beach fantastic, resort grounds very nice. Food ok, not as good as last trip. Not as much selection I guess. We got tired of the buffet after a couple days. We did the Italian and the Steak house, both pretty good. All in all, we still had a great trip, just not as 5 Star as the Grand Palladium. But taking the kids there would have been considerably more $$$$. Excursions: We did the Outback Safari, 2nd time with this company,(Peurto Plata 2001) we enjoyed this much more than the Monster Truck Safari-they just look after you better. Also did the Dolphin Island tour, quite an experience. More costly than Manati Park but apparently more time with the dolphins. Not much for English speaking staff here, they spoke more French and Spanish. Oh well the dolphins don't speak either, and that is why we went. They are truly beautiful, gentle creatures.This year we didn't take anything but American cash, we spent about 400.00 on bracelets, t-shirts, cigars, vanilla, coffee, coconut oil etc. More because of the kids of course. Lots of nice shops on Caribe Street, in the center of all the Riu's. Skyservice was fine, no leg room, but big plane, food was good cause we were starving!!! Our flight was two hours late leaving Punta Cana, we enjoyed the Wendy's at the airport very much. Almost exactly like home.So in summary, if you want 5 Star, book at the Riu Palace, or Grand Palladium Resort and Spa. IF you just want a clean friendly resort where the ocean is turquoise, the sand is soft and white, the Riu Taino will not disappoint.Shannon- Nipawin Sk, Cananda

<Author>ESCAPEWINTER2008
<Content>Enjoyed the Riu Taino We were thoroughly empressed with the Riu Taino! We went for a 2 week stay and were not disappointed! The airport was a bit confusing as far as not really knowing how to find our bus to take us to the resort. We sort of had to wander around with all of our luggage in a maze full of buses of various sizes in the airport parking lot. This was a bit frustrating but we finally managed to find the right one to take us to the hotel. The Riu was a 30 minute bus ride away. Once there the check in went very smoothly and we were even able to move to a room closer to our friends without a problem. The rooms were clean and more than sufficient. I'm not sure how much time people spend in rooms, but having a balcony a clean bathroom, a comfortable bed and airconditioning made this room wonderful. We enjoyed 2 weeks of sunshine and hot weather. The beach is breathtaking with soft white sand and extraordinary blue clear water. We spent most of our days laying on the beach chairs by the water and it was never a problem to get chairs. There were reefs close by that made for fun snorkeling--all kinds of neat fish that would come eat banana right out of your hand. The water is very clear so even if you don't have a mask (which you can also borrow from your resort) you can see the fish come up to the surface of the water for food. We took a catamaran out a few times and that was alot of fun. They are very easy to sail and don't take much skill. If you're nervous you can take a lesson for $25 but it was very easy to get the hang of so save your money and just give it a shot. You can use the catamarans, snorkeling equipment, windsurfers, paddle boats and kayakes for free. You just have to go up and book them (1 hour time slots) with the people at one of the booths. There were a bunch of beach vendors that were set up down the beach from our resort and we took many trips down the beach to do some shopping. Of course they insist they are giving you the very best price while all along quoting a price that is often 4 times higher than what you actually should pay. Haggling is the name of the game! There are lots of paintings, jewellery, sarongs, t-shirts, and wood carvings. We only did one excersion and that was the catamaran trip to Saona Island. This trip took us on an hour and a half bus ride to and from the pick up location. That part was exhausting. I didn't like spending 3 hours on a bus--even though it was air conditioned. The catamaran trip out to the island was really fun with music, dancing and lots of rum. Once we got to the island, it was rather disappointing. Although it is beautiful, it was no more beautiful than our own beach at the resort. It was apparently a little windy that day so it wasn't calm which is its claim to fame. Then we stopped at a natural pool on the way back in the motor boats, but really it was just an area of the ocean that didn't have waves. Boring! We did find one star fish there though. The a la carte restaurants were good and there was no limit as to how many times we ate at them which was probably 10 out of 13 nights. Our favourite was the Mexican restaurant where they made you fresh quesadillas. The steak house was good too and a bit of a surprise to have good steak while in the Dominican. The food at the buffets were more than adequate with lots of selection. I personally loved the fresh fruit smoothies blended every morning! I worked out in the gym and they had free weights as well as treadmills, steppers, and bikes. No airconditioning there only a few slow moving fans. But hey, it made me feel like I was really working hard with all the sweat pouring off of me! There is a street right next to the hotel called Caribe Street where there are all kinds of shops including clothing stores,painting store, a drug store, a confectionary (chips $5, chocolate bars $3), bathing suit store, stores with blow kids toys and air mattresses. Many of the tourists came from Europe with very few from the States and about 20% from Canada. Many of the staff could speak some english or at least enough to communicate with one another. The bartenders at the La Bamba bar were exceptional and we made some good friends! The Domincans really love their sugar and the majority of their drinks were quite sweet which got a bit much after a few days there. Also, they only had Pepsi and being Coke fans, that was a little disappointing. We booked through Sunquest and they had a Sunquest rep there to help us with anything we needed. When it was time to go the airport to leave, we were supposed to check the Sunquest binder to see if our plane was on time and when we did, it said that the plane was on time so we went to the airport. We ended up waiting there an extra 3 hours for our plane which was really frustrating because those were 3 hours we could have hung on the beach instead of at an airport. All in all we would definitely go back to this resort and to this country. We would also book with Riu again in other countries as this resort met all of our expectations! If you are looking for a clean, safe, fun, beautiful resort that isn't stuffy or too upscale this is definitely the place for you. Regular people enjoying a great vacation!!

<Author>mailroom2008
<Content>Very Nice We stayed at the Riu Taino from Febrary 9 - 16. We are from Toronto Ontario, an early 20's couple on our first vacation together and travelling to the carribean for our first time. We travelled with Skyservice using Sunquest vacations and booked through Flight Centre. The flight left about an hour late and was pretty cramped. However, being 6ft tall this was expected. We were given the $10 travellers card before boarding the plane, I know some people had to pay this upon arrival at the Punta Cana Airport. Found our bus fairly quickly and waited awile for it to fill up. I had a problem with these fellow passengers as they complained that the air conditioning was on too high and asked for it to be turned off. Idiots. At least the Riu Taino was the first stop and took about 25 to get there. Looking at the small cities you pass in the bus makes you not want to travel far from the resort. Sketchy!! Check in was painless as it was 11pm at the time. Our bags were taken to our room which was a fair distance from the main lobby but it's so nice and warm out that it really doesn't matter. The rooms are nice enough. Very clean with everything you need. There is a safe in the room at no extra cost. The worst part of the room is the two twin beds pushed together. A queen or king size bed would be nice. Fairly stiff bed and pillows but that didn't bother me. The bathroom was small but how much room do you need? There were a couple really small ants in the bathroom but they were no match for my human size finger. OK the best part. The beach is outstanding. I would like someone to show me a better beach than this. Very hard to top. Soft sand, warm clear water, and enough beach chairs to go around. The beach is a little cramped at the Taino however we spent most of our time at the Bambu beach as it's much larger with more chairs. The pool at the bambu is much larger as well, along with the swim up bar there. It's a little smaller at the Taino. It was 28C everyday before the humidex, hardly cloudy at all, and it rained every day for 2 minutes at night. We didn't see any shows at the indoor Taino ballroom because it was very smokey in there and we preffered to be outdoors so we went to the bambu every night. The break dancers were the best show for sure. Outstanding! Overall the food was ok. We did NOT get sick however we were scarred from stories of other guests who got sick which made us very nervous the whole week. So we were very picky when meant we got very bored of the food. There is a HUGE selection at every meal and if we weren't worried about getting sick we would not have been bored I'm sure. The service at Taino and Bambu were alright. Some people were good, others didn't care. I only tipped the ones who actually made an extra effort. Finally, I would stay here again for sure although I'd try to book at the bambu. I think we will try a different country altogether next time but I would trust staying at the other Riu's available down south. Unless you're a super snob and only stay in luxary don't go here. If you're a normal person who wants a nice vacation on the beach then I absolutley recommend this place! AND HAVE FUN.

<Author>travelcouple-0
<Content>Good place, great beach, food not so good My husband and I stayed at the Riu Taino from January 4th to 12th. All in all, it is a good place.Beach: Great white sand, clear blue water with great sunrises! A good idea is to walk to the Riu Bambu a two minute walk away, the beach is nicer and wider than Taino and you can use the Bambu's facilities as well. The beach can get pretty crowded but that's the game with all-inclusive resort areas, we always found a nice place to lay and bake. There was also lots of shade if that's what you're looking for.Staff: Nice. They all work very hard and long hours. The animacion team beats out the energizer bunny, we were wondering if it's really a natural high, for someone to go go go from 5 am to 2 am all the time is pretty awesome but crazy as well. But, they seem to enjoy their work.Rooms: The rooms are pretty basic but it was all we needed, clean bed, clean shower (with big time water pressure and never ran out of hot water). The mini fridge is funny, it's quite old and the door would fall off when we would open it, but we simply placed it back and laughed. It's a dated resort and needs some fixing. We did see some little tiny bugs at the door of the bathroom (ants I think) but the maid cleaned everything everyday and they were still there. What can you do, you are in the tropics. They didn't bother us or go anywhere else in the room, just don't leave food or drinks laying around in the room. The patio is great, pretty big, very clean and we had a great banana tree view.Grounds: Very clean and always trimmed. There was a cat walking around, he/she was cute, named him P'tit Gris (little gray).Pools: The smaller pool at the Taino is a bit dated but so is the rest of the resort. We still spent lots of time there since it's so close to the rooms, the bar, the bathrooms and the restaurant. It's all right there. We didn't go to the bigger pool bar but it seemed nice.Food: Hmm, not great, not terrible, but not great. I came to the conclusion that I might be a picky eater. The restaurants weren't great either, my husband got sick after the Italian restaurant and our friend got sick after the Mexican restaurant. The Chinese was probably the best and it wasn't great. I was sick at the end our of trip, stomach cramps and fever, not sure what it was but it wasn't fun. I understand the concept of the food in the islands (not the best) but I've had much better food at other resorts in the Caribbean. You won't starve that's for sure, but....blurk. Let's just say I ate lots of fries. The drinks are ok, the fruity ones are VERY sweet so if you're not into beer I recommed the Santo Libre (sprite with rum). Yes, the sprite IS less sweet than the fruity drinks! But it's all good. Drink the wine out of a jug or the champagne and you'll be great.Excursions: We did the Monster Truck Safari, loved it. If you want culture, breath taking natural beauty and fun, go. You drive through the town of Higuey, so you get to see the town and their ways (outdoor meat market), and then drive about an hour into the jungle. All you can drink on the truck (better drinks than at the resort), great tour guide, and great food at restaurant in the middle of the jungle (again better than the resort). You'll visit a typical dominican house, a school, a cobble stone river, a sugar cane plantation, a [-] fight (they don't finish it, thank God!), and a coconut plantation. You'll learn lots about the Dominican. Bring gifts for the kids if you can, they are so appreciative of anything. When a 5 year old is excited about tooth paste, it doesn't take much. We brought loads of teddy bears and they loved them.In the end, Riu Taino was fun, a great get-away vacation and cool since you can use the Riu Bambu next door. We wouldn't stay there again because we don't expect to return to Punta Cana, after seeing it once, it's enough (not much to do there) and we prefer to explore other areas. Honestly, the Riu Bambu had the best beach on the strip but it's not worth paying more to go to the Bambu, just walk there. We prefered the cheaper Taino, the patio in the room is better, the accomodations are the same at both resorts and so is the food.Just enjoy and have fun!  
<Date>Jan 21, 2008

<Author>Lillabet54
<Content>Claims to be a 5 Star Hotel--False Advertising from London, OntarioWe stayed at this resort last week and just arrived home on Sunday evening.When you first enter the lobby of the Riu Taino, their front desk staff lead you to believe this hotel is the most friendliest hotel in Punta Cana, and you get a warm, fuzzy feeling. The property is well maintained and has an abundance of palms, tended flowers and grassy patches. We saw some peacocks wandering around. The beach is exquisite, very fine white sand, The sea warm and benign. Every morning I walked from 6:30 - 8AM and witnessed super efficient beach cleaners raking up seaweed from the tide and putting it in huge black plastic garbage bags. It was a very beautiful and peaceful time of day. The major pool scared me. People stayed in there longer than bladder control might extend. Heavy chlorine clouded it every night but I didn't feel like jumping in the next day and drinking at the in-pool bar!The food is fine if not particularly good. Breakfast was my favourite meal. Lots of fresh fruit, many varieties of eggs, deli meats, croissants, breads and freshly squeezed juices. Lunch and dinner served burgers, pasta, fries, rice, beans, chicken in various guises and always, a few kinds of pizza. Not inspiring but okay. Beer was cold and satisfying. Wine in casks was essentially not potable. Very inferior. Other booze not my thing when generic and served with sweet who knows what! Others seemed to be enjoying it plenty and plentifully!Front desk service was good. Especially Gregory. But all spoke English and were friendly and helpful.If you can stand the crowds, for a reasonably priced all inclusive I'd say it is pretty good.

<Content>Had A Fabulous Time, Returning in August We have just returned from a one week vacation at the Riu Taino. We stayed from June 23-30. That was great, as after a long day of travel we just wanted to get rid of our luggage and relax.FoodWe are picky eaters so I was a little worried but we were fine. There was always something on the buffet that we liked and we did not get sick. It does get repetetive after a few days, but we never did go hungry. We did not try any of the a la carte restaurants because we were busy with activities, but I heard from others that they weren't that great. The Rooms were bright and clean. Could use some updating and new pillows, but really how much time do you spend in your room. We left a $5.00 tip for the maid every day and always had some nice towel art to return to. The room was always thoroughly cleaned and there was never an issue with hot water.Our fridge was stocked every couple of days with water, beer and soft drinks. Animacion staff were excellent, especially Charley, Kathy, Choco Andy, David and Rafael. The show's were very entertaining and we had a lot of fun participating in the daily dance classes. There was always something to do if you wanted and they didn't push you if you said no. These guys work so hard to keep everyone happy and entertained. The street party on Thursdays nights is a blast.The beach I would have to say is the most beautiful I have ever seen. Clean clear water and soft white sand. Just gorgeous.I would recommend the Monster Truck tour. It is a great way to see the real Dominican Life. Make sure to bring gifts for the children as they are always waiting at every stop. I would recommend the tour guide Joselito, he was great.We also did a speed boat/snorkelling tour through Bavaro Splash. It was a lot of fun getting to drive our own boat and the snorkelling spot was amazing, lots of fish. Make sure to bring an underwater camera.Great value for the money. You can also use the facilities at the Bambu and Naiboa, the casino at the Palace Macao and the Pacha disco (drinks are not included but the prices are not bad).As I said we had a wonderful stay, met some great people and are looking forward to our return on August 25.

We went to the quieter pool as we found the main pool with swim up bar a bit too busy and loud. The only trip we took was he Tropical Storm catermaran which i totally reccomend. A great day out, even got to see the nurse sharks (all be it through a net fence). Weather was great all week, sunny in the morning, bit cloudy in afternoons but enjoyed cloud as it was so hot. It rained and thundered and lightening some nights but nothing to moan about. All in all I would definately go back to the taino and also recomend to others. At the end of the day, you get what you pay for and as we got this holiday at a reasonable price, I was totally thrilled with it, cant complain, its what you make it.

<Author>shethinks
<Content>My first not so good review I've written several reviews here on Tripadvisor and always tried to be as honest as possible. And for the first time, my review won't be as positive as the others I've posted.Riu Taino is labelled as a 5 star hotel here in Europe. What is it that I didn't think it was worth five stars? Simple, here are the topics:- rooms very simple (i was prepared for that, because I had read all reviews before travelling).- on the first day, when we got to the room, the mini bar wasn't working (all drinks were warm) and the toilet didn't flush.-there was an invasion of dominicans and mexicans on Easter weekend. Suddenly, the main buffet Las Arecas, which was a quiet place turned into chaos and we found ourselves with queues of 30 people and very few things to eat (it was more than visible that the hotel had no capacity whatsoever to lodge that many clients).- The A la Carte restaurants, forgive me for saying this, were a joke. I only tried the Italian one, which had only 2 plates to chose from the menu and none had anything to do with italian cuisine. Worse was the fact that the food wasn't prepared at that time, and when it got to the table, the waiter said Wacth out for the plate, it's very hot ( the food had been warmed in the microwave oven).These were the most evident things. It's true that when we complained about the minibar and toilet, they sent someone to repair it, but this just shouldn't happen in a so -called 5* hotel.Everyone who worked there was nice, it's true. The beach was awesome, no doubt about it. I never went hungry, correct. The room was always very clean, also true. But to be honest, and after seeing (and eating at) the restaurants of Bambu and visiting Riu Palace Macao and the Palace punta Cana, I just feel that I could have made a better choice of hotels.Despite my choice of hotel, I enjoyed Dominican Republic very much, it has great beaches and the one of Taino is indeed great. Island Saona is something to die for and dominicans are simple and festive people. I will definitely go back but i think I will go to Gran Bahia Principe or a Riu Palace instead.P.S. For those who have already booked a stay at the Taino, I see no need in cancelling their trip. Just be prepared to the idea that the hotel has some flaws and it gives a service lower than five stars.Any questions, please email me, i'll be glad to answer all questions.

You could find yourself in a hospital with staff administering meds and you have no understanding of what you're getting. Spanish is the official and only language medical staff are allowed to use in the Dominican. I like the Dominican people. I think there are other good resorts. This one seemed poorly managed. Taking precautions, a person could enjoy Dominican. Choose a resort with raving reviews. Look closely at the bad reviews. As for us, we won't be going back to the Dominican. We'll stick to the english speaking islands. I'm just glad to be back home. It's made me realize how wonderful our food standards are here in Canada.

<Author>Boopoopydoo
<Content>Mixed Feelings My boyfriend and I traveled to the DR from March 9-14 for a short getaway from the daily grind of the East Coast. Where to begin? Before we left, we read these reviews religiously, and I will attempt to make this entry as helpful and honest as possible for whoever is traveling to this resort next. Overall, we truly enjoyed our stay. The people were great, the staff was very friendly, and the entertainment staff really did work hard to keep us engaged and entertained. The drinks were great, the beach was beautiful, and overall we're really satisfied with our vacation. The food: if you love meat, look before you eat, numerous times I cut into a piece of chicken and it was still pink. Also, we discovered that we could walk to the Riu Bambu up the beach for dinner! You should also explore Taino when you first arrive, we discovered two restaurants and another buffet place to eat on our 2nd to last day there. The resort: While Taino has the best beach access from the resort, Riu Bambu had a much more fun and lively crowd for us, especially since we are in our early 20's! We even got to dance under the stars to a live musical performance. : ) Also, the sunrise is gorgeous so try to wake up to see it one morning! My boyfriend and I love to take photos, so it was a great opportunity to take some great shots. The people: Lots of Europeans who like to wear Speedo's and go topless on the beach. Everyone was really fun loving though, which made it pleasant!VERY IMPORTANT: When it comes to the trips that the resort or your travel agent may recommend that you take, BE AWARE! We went on a day trip to SAONA ISLAND, a secluded island where we would be given unlimited alcohol and enjoy a bbq lunch on the beach, and were sorely disappointed by (1) the fact that it took 5+ hours to just get to and from the island itself, (2) the unlimited alcohol was just Rum and Coke, and what they call mamajuana and (3) the food made my boyfriend so sick that he has spent the past 12 days in the hospital (he just got out, which is why this review has taken so long for me to post). We think he caught something from the pork he had on the beach, or the fruit he had been eating, but we aren't sure. All we know is, he was fine before we went, and extremely sick the day after. The trip cost us $80 each and in our opinion, was NOT worth it, especially after the illness. ALSO (possibly even more) MPORTANT: DO NOT DO NOT DO NOT drink the water, don't even brush your teeth with it. People get really sick from it, and it just isn't worth it. Shopping: Shop AT THE RESORT SHOPS on Carribean Street at Taino- DONT buy stuff from the vendors who sell things in the lobby, because they are there to rip you off, AND the hotel doesn't even endorse their products. We bought some rum from one of the guys, and he started at $40 a bottle, and we went to caribbean street and found the same bottle for about $12. So (1) bargain with them, and (2) don't bother getting it if the price doesnt seem right, you'll find it cheaper in the shops. Also, the stores at the end of the beach have some cute stuff but be careful they will pounce on you to buy things the moment you look in their direction! Airport: Don't let people grab your bags, you will have like 6 people come try to help you and then you will have to tip each of them because they won't leave UNTIL you do! We carried our own bags, and never had that problem, but saw another couple who had 4 bags and were attacked by helpers. The bright side is, if you hate carrying your own bags, someone will be there to help you out : )Lastly, the ROOMS: Yes, the beds are hard, yes the sheets are course, yes they are a little outdated, and yes there are some mosquitoes in the room. SO: if you are particular about that kind of thing either (1) find another hotel with better beds and newer rooms, or (2) tire yourself out SO MUCH throughout the day that you will forget how uncomfortable the bed is! Also, if you leave money laying around in your room, your cleaning person may think its a tip for them (this happened to us with a few pesos), so be aware of that!DONT FORGET TO BRING: pepto bismol (it costs $9 on the resort!), bug spray (to fight those mosquitoes), and sun block (there were some REALLY red people). Also, the CDC says Punta Cana is a high risk area for malaria, so talk to your doctor if you want to be overly cautious. I would do that if we went again to that area. To sum up, would we go again? Probably not. Would we recommend the place? If you're looking for a few days of RR, a ladies week away, or just a budgeted vacation, then definitely. If you're planning a honeymoon, look elsewhere... heck, look at a different country, I hear Vancouver is pretty awesome. And you can drink the water. Contact me if you'd like photos or more information! We'd be happy to provide you with any help we can : ).

<Author>JPrev
<Content>Excellent trip!!! Our party consisted of two couples from Michigan and one from Delaware. All in our early 40's. This was our first trip outside of the States and wasn't sure what to expect based on the reviews.Flight: We flew Delta from Detroit to Atlanta to Punta Cana. The flight was uneventful. The fun began once we arrived at Punta Cana. It took about 1/2 hour from the airport to the resort. I will never again complain about road conditions in Michigan. Aggressive driving is apparently a way of life in the Dominican. I'm just now getting the feeling back in my thigh from my wife's death grip from our driver weaving in and out of traffic. The Punta Cana drivers would do well in the Nascar series.Rooms: The rooms were very clean. There were two beds, a full size and a single. They were a little hard but certainly sleep able. The mini bar was stocked with rum, vodka, gin, and brandy. The fridge was stocked with 4 Brahma beers, diet and regular Pepsi, tonic water and club soda. They also included 1 gallon of potable water. The tv also featured some American stations. Food: Overall, the food was good. Breakfasts consisted of eggs to order, bacon, sausage, fresh fruit, bakery items, juices. Lunches included fish, chicken, hot dogs, burgers, fries, fruit, salads etc... Dinners offered the greatest diversity. Sea food, steak, chicken, and pastas could be found on a nightly basis. They also offered Mexican, Italion, and Carribean nights. Very good. I would recomend a place called Captain Cooks. It is a 20 minute bus ride and features all you can eat seafood and drinks. It is well worth the $55.00 a person. Drinks: I am an avid beer drinker. They offer two beers, Brahma(offered in a bottle in your room), and El Presidente(offered on tap at the bars). The Brahma is drinkable. They only bring you 4 every other day. I quickly found out that you could walk down to there supply room and tip them ($2.00) to bring you more. They also appreciate chewing gum. The other option is El Presidente. If they offered warm Pabst Blue Ribbon that had been sitting out in the sun for 4 weeks, I would choose that over an ice-cold El Presidente!!! We often joked about the El Presidente smile. After taking a big gulp of the vile brew, think of ones facial expression when biting into a lemon, thus, the El Presidente smile. Took the Bubba Keg idea that we picked up from other reviews. One of the best tips we received.Tips: We initialy tipped the maid $5.00. We then tipped in candy, gum, coloring books and crayons. We always had fresh towels and a very clean room. It made no difference to tip the folks that restock the minibar. If you walk down to their booze bungalow, tip them there. I would recommend tipping the bartenders. We picked one out, Juan, and he was great. I would start to get out of my seat and he would already be making my drink. Staff: They were outstanding! They all seemed to be in there 20's and would go out of there way to try and please. Our second day there, I asked if we could move closer to the pool/ocean. Gregory put us in the building closest to the ocean and pool. I tipped him $20.00 after he delivered. We never encountered a language barrier. Beach/pool: The beach is beautiful as is the pool. There is a large ship that sunk about 1/2 mile out that is very interesting. I snorkeled every day. The reef is about 50 yards out and well worth the effort. I would bring bananas out with me and be swarmed with fish. There were normally 10 species of fish ranging from a couple inches to 18-24 inches. Very cool!!! I would recomend that you get up early and reserve your chairs by placing a towel over them. They tend to fill up quick. Also, bring a beach towel from home. Keep in mind that the majority of beach goers are non North Americans and many choose not to where tops. A good look on some...Shopping: We walked the 2 miles down the beach to bargain with the locals. Be prepared to battle. They are very aggressive and you definitely have to put on your game face. The booths sell basically the same merchandise. T-shirts, jewlery and cigars. We found out later that the cigars are packaged under false Cuban labels. For the few bucks that you might save, you might as well shop on the resort. Overall: We had a great time and will probably go back in the future.Have any questions contact me at japrev@jamadots.com

<Author>ilrusso
<Content>Great Time Just returned from an 8 day stay at the Taino. My husband and I travelled with another couple, and we are all in our mid to late 20's. My husband and I travel extensively, and have stayed at other all inclusive's including IBB next door (which we loved), Palladium Nuevo Vallarta, Riu Ocho Rios, Riu Jalisco, Punta Cana Princess. We booked this vacation because we were looking for a cheap get away, and this only cost $950 including flight and taxes a person. If we would have paid more we would have been extremely upset, but for that price we got what we paid for.   Let me start of by saying, this is NOT A FIVE STAR resort!!! It is not sold as such in the US, but I guess it is being advertised as such in Canada, if you go here expecting 5 stars you will be disappointed.  Upon arrival to the hotel, we were given 2 rooms (861-862), the rooms themselves were ok but they were way too far from everything. We asked to be moved and were told that the resort was full and they couldn't move us. After a $20 to Montero at the front desk, we had two great new rooms 224 and 204, both on the second floor, and very conveniently located. Note, these rooms were not in the old Melao section, they were Taino rooms. You will know the difference by the buildings, in Taino the buildings are smaller and different colors, in the old melao section the buildings are all the same beige color. Our flight was cancelled due to the weather in NY and Apple paid for us to stay an extra night, however, we had already checked our from our rooms and the new rooms were in the old Melao section (1105-1110). The rooms were disgusting!!! They had the worst mold smell I have ever smelled, it was so bad my lungs hurt. There was no balcony, and you couldn't open windows as there was no nets to keep the bugs out We spent the week relieved that we would come home without the moldy hotel smell on all our clothes, as our rooms didnt smell at all. Well, the last night in the old Melao rooms sure made up for that. Stay away at all costs, when you check in ask where your room will be if it is in a location you dont like (check the map at the front desk) or an old Melao room, slip a $20, and they will promptly find you a better room.Food: I have never seen so little food at an all inclusive before. There was really very little variety, and very few edible dishes. We did find something to eat, but I actually came home 4 pounds lighter. If food is very important to you, I would not go to this resort. Also, during the day you can have breakfast and lunch at Bambu, next door, do so as there is more variety at their buffets than in Taino.Entertainment: I didnt really care for the shows much. I didn't expect Broadway, but there shows are really worse than what we have seen in other resorts, most of the show they do not even bother to translate into English, speaking in Spanish, German and French instead. But the bars were always a great place to hang out at night, as there was lots of people hanging out until early morning. Disco was fun as well.In the past I have read the reviews that described this place as Hedonism 4, due to the debauchery that allegedly went on. I did not see any nude women (or kids for that matter), although there was a lot of topless sunbathing. Also, I didn't see anyone behaving inappropriately, while we were there there was a huge group of Spanish spring breakers, and they were all extremely well behaved.Overall, I booked this hotel for dirt cheap, and I feel like I got what I paid for (which was not a lot). We had a great time, the drinks were great, the beach was gorgeous, and the aquatic tour we took was a blast.Tip: If going to this resort, go riu.com and sign up for the RIU card, it will give you discount on the internet (50% off), and 25% of at the spa, as well as some discounts at other shops.

<Author>Danvers07
<Content>A great vacation for the price We went to Punta Cana on the spur of the moment Feb 11-18, 2007 after seeing sale prices in our local newspaper.  After checking Trip Advisor reviews our expectations were modest and we were pleased that the Riu Taino exceeded our expectations in almost all ways. We were greeted promptly on check in, and 5 minutes later were escorted to our room. Although a long way back in the resort the grounds were beautiful, the room was spotless, and very quiet. As reviewed the beds were extra firm and the pillows slim. Due to the high humidity you had to run the air conditioning all the time to try and keep things dry. No big deal, this is the tropics, 85 degrees, sunny, and humid 7 days in a row. The room was cold at night and we asked for a blanket, you could have slept outside in Maine in winter with the blankets they supplied, no use in the islands.  The beach was beautiful and you could walk for miles past the other resorts and check them out. There was no beverage service on the beach, but you could take a short walk up to a bar and get whatever you wanted. The bar had plenty of help and it was never more than a few minutes to get a drink. There was no food service on the beach, but again it was a short walk away. The food on the buffet could have been better, but if you couldn't find something at each meal to enjoy you were just being too picky. Lighten up and have a good time. Every evening there was steak, chicken, 2-3 types of pasta, ribs, fish, and shrimp for entrees, and then 30-40 breads, fruits, veg, and deserts. Bar service in the restaurants was limited to beer and wine. The white wine could double for vinegar in the salad area, so stick to the red. The Italian restaurant was bad, poor qlty, limited true Italian entres, the wait staff wanted to take your meal and desert selections nearly the moment you walked in the door.  The 7 PM seating in the Steak house was one of the best meals of the week, and when the staff found out it was our wedding anniversary they gave us a bottle of champagne. Our waiter made sure our water and wine was refilled without making a fuss. Don't go to the 9 PM seatings, everything is dried out because they cook all the food earlier. Take a walk down the beach and reserve free use of the Hobie Cat catamarans. The winds are brisk in the afternoon and if your heading towards shore and riding a breaking wave it's just great fun. If you go expecting a 5 star experience when you are paying 40-50% less at the Taino than at the other resorts your bound to feel let down. A smile, a few $$ for tips, and an attempt to throw in a few words of spanish makes for better service and a more enjoyable experience. Remember the staff is trying to understand German, French, Dutch, English, and Spanish.

<Content>Absolutely Delightful!!! I stayed at the Riu Taino on February 20th -27th with my husband, my parents, and my brother and his wife. We had an excellent time at the Dominican. It was the first time I've stayed at a Riu hotel, and I must say it is 'top notch'.Here's my overall review from the flight to the food to the beach:Flight: We travelled with Skyservice. Being 5'10'' myself and my husband being 6'4'', we found it very uncomfortable. The seats were cramped with absolutely no leg room. My 5'0'' sister in law also found it tight herself. Other than that, it was a safe smooth ride to beautiful Punta Cana.Arrival: As we arrived to the Punta Cana airport we got out luggage and boarded our Coco Tours bus in a matter of 20-30 mins - and then we were off to the Riu Taino.Hotel: The first impression of the hotel was the size. It is pretty grand - including it's own street 'Caribbean Street'. As we got there at around 11:30, we were informed that the hotel room would not be available until 1 p.m. - they informed us that we could leave our baggage there or within their office and go and have some drinks and lunch. We arrived back at the front desk at around 1:15 and our rooms were ready. The busboy helped us take our luggage to our rooms.The Room: The rooms were 'ok'. Despite being a little dated, it was extremely clean. There were always clean linen, towels, etc everyday. They even made some cute ducks? or was it snakes? - not sure, out of towels and the little red flowers located throughout the hotel compound. There's a safe deposit box in each room. Each safe had a separate barrel; therefore, it would be impossible for anyone to break into your safe. The fridges were always stocked with cold beer and soda pop - and the 4 litre jug of water. There were never any roaches, ants or other insects in our rooms.The Beach: Absolutely beautiful. That's the reason we visited Punta Cana again. You can walk for miles along the beach and visit the other Riu hotels. The Food: My favourite part! Being from the Caribbean myself (West Indian) we enjoy a little spice in our food. Breakfast, lunch and dinner were exceptionally great. We visited one of the a la carte, but it happens to be a buffet as well, so it wasn't much different. The main buffet suited us just fine. We were served fresh seafood almost everyday. From lobster, crabs, calamari, fish, shrimp, you name it! One day they had stewed beef and rice - delicious. The desserts were plentiful - from pastries, to cakes to freshly cut fruit. My favourite was the sour sap and papaya. The Pizza: I've had pizza at many different resorts in the caribbean, this one is my favourite. The cheese pizza is absolutely delicious.Overall, the Riu experience was absolutely great. I would definitely return to the hotel in the future.

<Content>Riu Taino a very nice holiday I just arrived home from the Riu Taino yesterday and had a wonderful time. I'd like to address some of the things I read in past reviews about this hotel. It's true that they put corn and weiners on pizza but they also had many other varieties so you didn't have to choose it if you didn't wish to. We had no problems with bugs or flies at any time on the resort or near the food. The staff was very helpful and the Animacion team worked very hard to entertain. The pools were also very nice and never in my time there did I smell sewage by the pool bar as had been reported. The one complaint that I have is that they will not let you change your wet beach towel in for a dry one on the same day. One towel per person per day is the allotment. To get around this we simply had one person take the towel back and obtain the card and sent another of our party to retrieve a new towel. All in all I have tosay that my holiday was a success and worth the money spent.

<Author>Torontonian123
<Content>Nice beach but that's about all. We stayed at the Riu Taino from Jan 20-27th. No welcome drinks, which would have been nice since we arrived late in the evening after a very cramped flight. We were directed to a snack bar area for food which had obviously been sitting there for hours and was barely edible. Our rooms were ready right away but they were some distance away from everything so we spent a lot of time walking everywhere we had to go. It鈥檚 nice to walk but gets tiresome after a while, especially if you have young children with you. I鈥檇 request a room closer to the lobby if I were to go again. Rooms: Apparently there are no adjoining rooms but they did put our three rooms in the same building, which was fine. My husband and I would have preferred two doubles or one king bed rather than a single and a double, but we made do. Otherwise the rooms are clean, air conditioning works fine and there's also an overhead fan. Plenty of closet space. Bathroom was clean although a cabinet would have been nice. Yes there was paint in the tub but who cares? It was clean. The shower in our washroom was broken so we had to hold the shower head in our hands to shower, which was a bit of a drag. The showers in the other two rooms worked fine and they have good water pressure. The rooms, bedding and pillows did not smell moldy but they were definitely old and dated and occasionally stained. It鈥檚 time they invested in new beds and bedding. Pillows were really flat but we brought our own so we were ok. The rooms were cleaned beautifully every day and we always received towel art. The maids appeared to be cleaning rooms all day and into the evening. We came and went as we pleased and the rooms were always done by the time we came back. Bugs: We got mosquito bitten quite a bit and there we鈥檙e also plenty of 鈥渘o-see-ums鈥?feasting on our legs on the outdoor patios at night, so bring bug spray. We killed 10 mosquitoes in our room one night. They hide in the curtains. Food: We ate our main meals at the main reception buffet all but one night. Although there was a variety of food, it was all very bland and there was something about it that just didn't sit well with me. I'd take about 4 bites then couldn't stomach any more. I survived on bananas, soup and cantelope for the most part. Yes, they always had hotdogs and burgers (neither of which were edible in our books) but they also had caviar, fresh breads, desserts, shrimp, lobster, roast pork, roast lamb, salads galore etc. You won鈥檛 go hungry but eating was definitely not a highlight of this trip. Be careful of the roast chicken as it was not cooked enough at all. If you鈥檙e taking children, supervise their choices carefully. A lot of the food is recycled, not heated enough or past it鈥檚 time. A lot of flies around the food at all buffets. They should cover the food better. Just use common sense and you shouldn鈥檛 get sick. Previous reviews generally correct about the food: fried eggs are runny and overcooked on the bottom, bacon and sausages were either overcooked or undercooked and very greasy, undercooked scrambled eggs with a variety of leftovers thrown in etc. We enjoyed fresh fruit smoothies. No cereal. No cold milk. Toast with jam was a staple. We booked the Italian restaurant for 7 and found they had booked the steakhouse restaurant for 9 instead, which was disappointing. The steakhouse was a joke. We were first in line for our sitting and we were served last. The main course took an hour and twenty minutes to arrive and they made no apologies whatsoever. Both the service and the main course were terrible. The steak was boiled prime rib that was unceremoniously thrown on a plate with some three day old vegetable mush that was equally unedible. Some of us got a golf ball sized baked potato but they were not cooked so you couldn鈥檛 eat them either. The main course was simply not tolerable. The only saving grace was the salad buffet where we managed to fill up on nachos, guacamole and a few other items you get at the main buffet anyway. We didn鈥檛 book to eat at any of the other ala carte restaurants after that. We had intended to eat at the Riu Bambu one night but never got around to it. The buffet may be slightly better there from what we saw of it but don鈥檛 quote me on it. Avoid the steakhouse at all costs. If the pasta that is available at the buffets is any indication of the pasta at the Italian restaurant, I wouldn't bother going there either. At least at the buffets you have more options.Drinks were great - anything you want is there for the asking. Ask for premium liquor as they do have it. I enjoyed the gin and tonics or scotch on the rocks. Service at the bars was always good even when crowded. They鈥檙e not cheap with the shots. Nice bartenders, tip them occasionally. Opt for cappuccino at the coffee machines. I often poured it over ice in a glass for a cold coffee. You can get a few extra beer for the frig in your room if you tip the boys who deliver it for you. Would have been nice to have access to some ice for mixed drinks in our rooms but no big deal. Staff: We loved Pedro!!! He made our trip with his amazing sense of humor. He really knows how to keep people laughing. Do whatever he asks you to participate in and you鈥檙e sure to have fun. We played volleyball and a Frisbee game with him. We thought he was the best dancer on the entertainment team too so don鈥檛 miss out on dance nights at the Bamboo bar. We spent all of our time at the beach so we didn鈥檛 really meet the rest of the entertainment team because they work in the pool areas. The rest of the staff were always pleasant and efficient. If you want a siesta in the afternoon, be advised that the maid staff all have walkie talkies on loud and they yell back and forth to each other throughout the day. You鈥檙e better off snoozing on the beach rather than attempting to sleep in your room.The beach: Beautiful blue water and very soft sand. Definitely the highlight of the trip. It was busy but not overly crowded. Plenty of room to stroll the beach. We always found chairs and we never had any problems getting towels at any time of day. There were topless women but we didn鈥檛 see any explicit behaviour. Water was cooler than Mexico but refreshing. You can get some snorkeling gear free and see some small fish around the reefs there. You can bargain them down from $95 to $65 for two for parasailing, just tip the rep a bit. Big waves were not too suitable for smaller children who are not as water savvy. There was always a gentle breeze and the temperature was perfect. Bring a light sweater for the evenings, especially if you like to walk along the beach at night.The pools: We played water polo and it was great fun, but one of the guests seriously cut the bottom of his foot on the bottom of the pool. It ruined the rest of his stay. Guests: I found it hard to get a smile out of any of the guests. Most of them looked at me as if I had two heads when I smiled as we passed by each other. Not too many English speaking people there at all. A few families with toddlers. Many married couples aged 45 and up. Some small groups of young people but mostly 35+. I wouldn鈥檛 recommend this place for anyone who wants to stay up partying. There is a disco on the property where a lot of the staff frequent (and you have to pay for any drinks you want there) but all and all, this is more of a low key place where most people go to bed and rise early. Guests generally keep to themselves. Sunquest: Christine, our Sunquest rep, was supposed to meet us at 10:30 the morning after we arrived. After waiting an hour, the front desk informed us she wasn鈥檛 coming and to come back at 5:30. She never showed up both times. This was an inconsiderate waste of our vacation time. It also shortchanged us of a proper orientation and information about local excursions. We will do our best to avoid traveling with Sunquest again. Try and get all the info you need for excursions off of the Trip Central boards before you leave or you鈥檒l get ripped off. For example, we requested a snorkeling trip and they sent us to Sanoa Island. It took 3 hours on the bus and 1.5 hours on the catamaran to get out there. We spent only 2.5 hours on the island and there was no snorkeling whatsoever. Then we had to travel back by speedboat and bus. The island is beautiful but wasn鈥檛 worth wasting our whole day in traveling like that. The food they served at the island was barely edible and the servers were just short of rude. The beach at the resort is just as nice. Skyservice: Our flight back was delayed from 10pm until 2:30 am so we were utterly exhausted when we finally arrived home鈥efinitely not fun with children in tow. Do not let them put you in row 11 or in the rows next to the middle exit doors. We couldn鈥檛 sleep a wink on the plane because these seats do not recline back at all and when the passengers in front of us reclined their seats, we had no room to move at all. Tips: 1.) I would look into flights out of Buffalo rather than Toronto. Apparently it鈥檚 a lot cheaper and there are not as many delays. 2.) I would look into a resort with better quality food. Personally, not having to prepare meals and dining out is a big part of what us Moms enjoy about vacationing. They have a lot of food but it was not appetizing at all.3.) Bring snacks for your rooms if you鈥檙e bringing children. They spend a lot of time in the sun and exercising so they often need a healthy bedtime snack. 4.) Bring some staple drugs, such as cough medicine, Tylonol, polysporin, anti-scathing powder, Tums or Rolaids. They charge a fortune for these items in the gift shops. Extra bathing suits and sunhats for children recommended. Clothing does not dry as easily there.5) My husband was bitten fiercely by fire ants when he walked barefoot on the grass. Your feet get chewed up if you walk on the hot stone pavement for any length of time so be sure to bring comfortable shoes for walking the grounds. 6.) Absolutely make sure you have $20US per person when you arrive at the airport to leave. We were short $8 and the bank machine at the airport was out of order. They seriously will not let you on your plane unless you have every penny. We had to beg and plead incessantly to have someone escort my husband to another bank machine beyond the gates to get the balance of money we needed. In fact, I would get all the money you need before you leave as it鈥檚 not easy to access money there at all.10.) Jet fuel exhaust in the terminals is intense because it鈥檚 all open concept. Wait beyond the gates until half hour before you have to board.11.) Travel light. You鈥檒l be in your bathing suit all day and you鈥檒l only need some clothes for dining and dancing in the evening. Men must wear pants for dinner, no M shirts. If you plan on going on excursions you may want to bring some capris. 12.) Leave your jewellery at home. My rings loosened considerably in the salt water so I put them in the safe.

On our last stay, if a worker had even thought about talking rudely to a guest, the managers would have been all over the worker.The food....horrible. How do you mess up hot dogs and hamburgers, and pizza. The food was often undercooked and the bacon in the morning was either burned or completely raw. The food was horrible. We informed him that we had purchased the drink in the secure area, and he again stated that she had to get rid of the drink. The family that we met from England said that it is rated a 3-1/2 star resort in the English brochures. For the value it was a good vacation but we will look to stay at the Riu Palace next time.

<Author>GrandesAl
<Content>Beautiful Beach My friend and I spent a week at the RIU Taino from Nov 29-Dec 6. It was our first time to the DR and we enjoyed it. I am by no means an expert on resorts but I have stayed at all inclusives in Puerto Vallarta and Cabo but this was my first experience outside Mexico. The registering was a breeze as well as the transport from the airport (40 min.) The resort consists of rooms in 2 story bungalows scattered amongst beautifully maintained gardens. The room itself was basic. This time instead of having 2 double beds we had 2 twin beds. The beds were hard (of course) and the linens could have been updated. The A/C worked well and the room included a minibar and a liquor dispenser with bottles of rum, vodka, gin and brandy.. The minibar had a few beers and pop (mix). Unfortunately they are refilled every 2 days (twice during our stay) which isn't often enough but satisfactory. When you stay at the Taino you also have access to 2 other adjacent RIU properties. We never ventured off to explore the others as we found the bars and restaurants more than adequate at the Taino. There are 2 pools and each one had a bar access and a snack bar. The main pool had a swim up bar. There is no service on the pool decks so the bar service is self serve. The pools are beside the beach. The beach is awesome..beautiful white sand and turquoise water. There is a reef off shore that the waves break over. Awesome!!! The first few days were very windy so we spent our days sunning at the pool, the last few days the wind died right down creating a hot pool deck so we sat at the beach where the breeze was welcome and cooling. The activity staff poolside always had games and activities going on and always had a smile. They were awesome.  The food was typical of most buffets at resorts with great breakfasts and average lunches and dinners. The bars where I am an expert (I'm a bartender) were well equipped with a bigger selection than what I had seen previously. The bar staff were friendly and I made quick friends with a few of them. Augusto and Edwin at the Cocos Bar and Luis Miguel at La Bamba. Very few of the staff speak English but it gave me a chance to work on my Spanish. I thought I did quite well (Pat on back) It really isn't necessary for them to speak English as 90% of the clientele are European and seem to be able to speak Spanish. Augusto gave me a couple of CD's to take home. The biggest difference for me was the amount of Europeans compared to Mexico. I found it difficult to start up any conversations while sitting at the bar which is usually my specialty!! Of course that is not the fault of the resort, just a demographic.Due to the location of the resort (NE corner of the DR) there are no sunsets so I highly recommend getting up early and seeing the sunrise. Well worth it.I'd definitely go back to Punta Cana and the RIU resorts
