<Content>GOOD HOTEL BUT SOME PROBLEMS Hello: Husband and I just back from 8 days at the Riu Taino. I have left a review for the Riu Naiba - we checked out of that hotel and into the Taino. My husband is handicap and with cane so the first property is not on the beach and very hard for anyone with a walking problem. The Taino has a wonderful location. Very gorgeous property - right on the most beautiful beach I have ever seen. All the rooms are like little cottages/bungalow type style. Very pretty location. But the beds are all singles and we pushed them together to make one large bed. Sheets and covers are horrid - very old and ragged looking as well as the pillows. Hard to get a good night sleep but being on the gorgeous beach each day made up for this small problem. The property is beautiful but again very spread out. This is a hard place for anyone elderly or handicap. Be reminded you will do alot of walking. No easy way to get around. With that in mind this place is a gem! Food is wonderful - no one should ever complain on it. Fantastic. Good choices each and every night. Drinks are wonderful and non-stop all day. The staff is wonderful. The english language is a bit of a struggle so be prepared to learn your spanish fast. We were the only americans during the week of Oct. 8th but it was a wonderful experience to meet so many people from all over the world - mostly Spain, Brazil, Germany. I can't really complain on anything other than the beds and the walking. This is a great property, beautiful beach in the world, wonderful pool, great entertainment at night. You will enjoy yourself and not get bored. Just be prepared for the walking, not much english spoken and a bit of confusion on check-in but all in all - for the price - this is a great little spot. Please email if I can further assist anyone. Good luck and happy travels to all. Punta Cana is a wonderful, beautiful spot with beautiful beaches and great people!

<Author>Abiku
<Content>Awesome beach; good budget vacation experience We just returned home from a 6-day trip to the Riu Taino. This is our second time staying at a Riu All-Inclusive hotel (the first time was for our Honeymoon in Cabo San Lucas, Mexico.) Riu has a complex of six hotels in Punta Cana which provide accommodations for every budget. Ours was definitely the budget experience and if you choose to stay here, have no doubt that you will get what you pay for. Nevertheless, the Riu Taino is a very nice all-inclusive hotel for the budget-conscious traveler. But if you want to be pampered, go to the Riu Palace Macao instead!Accommodations: The rooms at the Riu Taino are in four-room bungalows (2 up; 2 down) The rooms are rather basic but fine. The cleaning lady showed up most every morning about 8:30 a.m., so you'd be smart to be an early riser. You'll get new drinks every 2 days in your minibar and you should ask for what you want. The parts that were a little annoying were the sheets (no fitted sheets so you would awake in the middle of the night with nothing between you and the mattress) and the towels (never enough for us two longhairs.) We probably ended up spending more time there than we would have planned (my husband got sick during the latter part of the trip; also they had WGN Channel 9 so we could watch the Chicago White Sox, our favorite baseball team ,while we were there.)Beach: What can I say? This is the reason to come to Punta Cana! The Riu is very well positioned on Punta Cana's beach. The white sands are complemented by gentle waves and warm waters. For sunbathers this is an exceptional place. The weather was wonderful, too. Not too hot (I don't think it got above 90 degrees the whole time we were there) and there was always a gentle breeze or even a good wind on some days. It rained intensely but briefly about every other day we were there. Be aware that the high number of Europeans who come to Riu Taino mean lots of topless sunbathing, so if this is a problem for you this is not the place to go on vacation.Food/Drink: The Riu all-inclusive plan offers a great deal of variety of foods at every meal. Dinner at the main restaurant is by reserved table, so don't forget to reserve your table your first day there! I would consider myself a real foodie, and while this is not a gourmet experience, the food is decent and most anyone will be able to find something they would be happy eating. Besides the main restaurant in the hotel lobby, there is also a snack bar, a pizzeria (one of our favorites for late lunch) and a couple of specialty restaurants (but we didn't visit them) Incidentally, the folks here have the food service down much better than the folks in Cabo, where the specialty restaurant reservations were a real hassle. Drinks are good, but vary in strength, so if you want it strong make sure to ask for it strong! The Mojitos were especially tasty!Service: The service was cordial and polite, but this is one area where a gratuity really makes a difference. We tipped bartenders, maids, waiters, bellhops, etc., but I don't recall seeing a single other person doing this! I think this is wrong. These folks work from sunrise to midnight, having to negotiate at least four languages on a daily basis and they deserve to be appreciated and treated with consideration. Make sure you tip!!!Entertainment: This is the area where Riu is really corny and weak! Merengue and Bachata music are terrific; fun to listen or dance to. But if you want the real thing, I suggest you get out of the hotel complex and go elsewhere to get the authentic experience. The shows at the hotel were really cheesy 鈥?Tribute to Michael Jackson? Cabaret a la Chicago? Come on! Maybe the Germans who were born before 1950 think this is exciting but for us, hip late-30-somethings, it was embarrassingly bad. This was to be expected because the entertainment at Riu's Cabo hotel was even worse! I do have to give it to the Animacion team, they conducted a great deal of daytime activities such as water polo, volleyball, dance lessons, etc. all day long before they prepared for the evening shows. They work hard and they do it in four languages!Shopping: Listen, don't bother going shopping at the Calle Caribena. Instead go to the artisan market on the end of the beach. It's a bit of a walk, but totally worth it! The paintings particularly are exceptional. You can take away some really special and unique souvenirs. There are a few services on the Calle Caribena that you might need: The Fitness Center, Spa, Pharmacy and Doctor. But otherwise, most everything is overpriced and can be sought elsewheere.Be careful with:鈥eing understood if you speak only English: English is the least common language heard at the Riu Taino. There are many more Spaniards, Germans and French there than anyone else. We really didn't encounter any other US citizens, though since I speak fluent Spanish we were always fine, but it seemed odd to hear only English once we got back to the US鈥?br/>鈥edding: It's especially bad. If you're a couple, forget about sleeping together. Just accept that you'll be sleeping separately and that you might not have fitted sheets on your bed.鈥each Towels: Make sure you get there by 10:00 a.m. They鈥檙e often out by then.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>beautiful beach We just returned from Punta Cana where the weather was gorgeous and the beach was the best we have every seen and we have been to Hawaii, Jamaca, Riveria Maya, Greece, Spain, California and many east coast beaches. We traveled with my three teenage children, my sister and her teenage son. All agree the beach was the best. Water sports were convenient and easy to obtain. We went snorkeling (free with the resort) with some interesting fish in the right corner of the swim area, kayaking (free with the resort), scuba diving (free trial in the pool, but extra to go on a dive) and parasailing (paid extra). If scuba diving remember to get a note from your doctor if you are taking any prescription medications!The accomadations were very nice. We liked the villa type accomadations (4 units per villa), but booking through Orbitz (even when we contacted the hotel 4 weeks prior to our arrival) we did not get all our rooms in the same building. Plus there are no connecting rooms which make it difficult for family travelers. The air- conditioning was great in all our rooms. The higher the room number, the less noice and traffic, but the maids came later (3-4 pm) at the high room numbers. Other reviews noted the pillows are all flat and there are no wash clothes. We concur, but we did not let this ruin our vacation. Food was very good in the dining area with a great variety. All the teenagers found something they liked and all had some foods/beverages that they have never had before. The food is very un-American, which was OK with us, but would be a problem for people who were reluctant to try new things. There were french fries and pizza available at each meal for the gastronomically impaired. There is an abundance of fruit, but the staple vegetables are cabbage and carrots. Which may have contributed to the loose stool problem experienced by 4 of 7 people in our party. Also the water from the tap is not drinkable. This was very hard to remember when you are brushing your teeth. Drinkable water is supplied in abundance, but it is hard to remember not to drink from the tap. We came prepared with an antidiarrheal medication. We did eat out at the restaurant for Carribean food and Steak and our whole group agrees that it was not as good as the buffet. We do not recommend the experience.The resort pool was very nice and the 14 year old boys spent most of their time at the pool, with the 18 year olds at the swim up bar with Hector. We always got loungers, but it was a little competative by the pools particularly on Fridays and Saturdays. There were always lounge chairs on the beach with lots of palm trees to rest under. The Entertainment crew was very enthusiastic and multiligual. We attended one show, the kids loved the bingo and watched some poolside programs. They were good -- the usual quality for the resort. Probably 25% of the resort guests were from English speaking countries. We are used to travel in Europe, but if you are not then the fact that English is not the primary language can be a bit of a challenge. We did not go off the resort this trip and still found plenty to do. There does not appear to be a children's program and there were not a lot of teenagers at this resort. That was nice for us, because it was truly a family vacation, but the teenagers said they would like to come back with a group of friends!

<Content>Disapointed with Riu As a four time visitor to the Dominican Republic, but a first time visitor to the Riu, I was not impressed. The beach is excellent, but beyond that it appears that you have paid for the Riu name and not quality or service. The rooms were acceptable but new larger beds could be purchased. Luckily they were leaving the next day and of course as they took over the resort area they did provide us with our nightly entertainment. Which brings me to entertainment. When you have visitied DR more than once you understand that the audience participation portions of a show will always be included, but with the Riu it was basically the entertainment. Nor do I want to constantly hear a live advertisement because I did not find myself actually wanting to jump on the I want to go to Riu bandwagon. There were a few optional bits and pieces thrown in, but nothing that would make you look forward to the night's scheduled entertainment. And the party on Carribean Street, just a ploy to get you to shop Carribean Street. Service was also an issue. I do not expect continual above excellence, but when I request a cup of coffee with milk in Spanish it would have been nice that the server understood my request as well as brought the beverage. I also witnessed a repeat visitor (8 times) ask the restaurant manger for coffee since the server was not available, he also did not get his coffee that evening. Needless to say, I went home with a bunch of ones still in my pocket. As I mentioned, the beach was excellent and that was this resorts only saving grace. I had read the reviews and spoke with a two timer before choosing the Riu and thought I had made a good choice, but we have crossed this resort off of our repeat visit list.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>We'll be back! We went on a fabulous trip to the Riu Taino. From the moment we checked in to the moment we checked out it was a wonderful vacation and one I hope to do again. To break it down:Room: Yes the beds were a bit hard and the rooms could use a little updating, but really we spent about 9 hours in our room per day...8 sleeping and 1 taking showers and getting ready. Who goes to paradise to sit in a hotel room? We were so tired at night that we fell right asleep. Food: The food was good, there was always something we could find that we liked. I didn't plan on going there and eating like I do in the states. The breads, cheeses, pizza, fruit and vegetables were always good. The breakfast was great; I had an omelette each day. The best part.... no one in our party was ever sick! We each drank lots of water in the morning, alcoholic beverages in the afternoon and evening and we were fine.Beach/Pool: The beach is absolutely beautiful. When you see a picture of paradise, I believe they take the picture in Punta Cana. The sand is white and soft and the ocean is turquoise blue. We didn鈥檛 see any high rises so the tallest things along the beach are palm trees.The pools were all beautiful. We stayed at the Taino but also visited the Naiboa pool one day. It was quieter at the Naiboa pool but both were wonderful. You do have to hunt a bit for a chair at the Taino because there are many people who put their towels on their chairs and then don't sit there much. We didn't really have much of a problem hauling chairs around so they would be next to each other.Employees: The people of the Dominican Republic are very kind and friendly people. When I read reviews of people complaining about them not speaking English I find it so frustrating as we are in their country. Is each employee suppose to know 4+ languages? Believe it or not鈥ome do. The guests at the Riu were from all around the world, and we heard many languages being spoken, which was part of the interest of the whole trip. I speak English, know a little French and an even smaller amount of Spanish but did not find it to be a hinderance. Give Spanish a try and know the basics and it will be of great help. Advice:-Go to the Dominican and the Riu with an open mind, you will have a wonderful time.-I would give our housekeeper a couple dollars a day and a $1.00 gift from Target. We also tipped the bartenders, the waiters/waitresses, etc...however no one ever seemed to expect it or ask for it.-Bring an insulated mug ie..Bubba Keg. We were told by a very nice guest from Canada that she brings a few each trip and gives them as gifts to the hotel employees.-Souvenir buying-go down to beach shops and pay about 30% of what they originally tell you the price is. The shops on Caribbean street have set prices, so you will pay more but if you don鈥檛 like bartering this might be more for you.

<Author>MALMN
<Content>Great Time at the Riu Taino We stayed at the Riu Taino from 2/20/06-2/27/06 and I must say I was pleasantly surprised by what a great experience we had. We went to Punta Cana after much research, but we were still nervous about the hotel and not knowing what to expect, but it was just great. When we checked in, the front desk clerks were very friendly. Ernesto is an absolute doll and would say hello to us throughout our entire stay, always remembering our names which was so nice. The rooms were a bit dated, but very clean. The maid service was always great and the bungalow style of the rooms is a refreshing change from the typical highrise hotel. The beach is absolutely spectacular. Probably the most beautiful beach I've ever seen. The sand was soft and not rocky at all. The water was so blue and also was not rocky at all. Simply wonderful. The pools at the hotel were very nice and the pool bar always proved to be entertaining. It is quite difficult to get a chair by the pool though. People would get up at the crack of dawn and lay their belongings on a chair in order to save it for later. This could be annoying, but we could always find a chair at the beach, and after searching hard, we could usually find one at the pool. Because of the fact that the Naiboa is not on the beach, people from this resort would come over to the Taino's pool and beach. The option to travel to the other Riu's was an added bonus. We really enjoyed the bar at the Bambu, bartender Ray was simply the best! He was constantly bringing us drinks and such a cutie. There is a nice brick path connecting all the Riu hotels which runs along the beach, so you can simply hop on the path and go from hotel to hotel, which makes it so easy. Even at night, this path was very well lit and we felt totally safe. And finally, the food. People complain about food so much and my personal opinion is: get over it! It's an all inclusive at a reasonable price, the food is not going to be what you would get at a 5 star restaurant. Overall, the food was what you would expect, kind of bland, but there was always something you could find that was good. It was a bit repetative, but compared to other all inclusives I have stayed at, it was much better. There was always a large selection and everything was usually very fresh. I would stick with the buffets though, we went to the sit down restaurant and it was horrible. And unfortunately all the Riu hotels in the complex tend to have the same menu and choices, so even though you can eat at all of them, they're more or less the same. I also agree with other reviews though, bring a big insulated mug, it will help keep the beer cold! This is getting to be a long review so I will just add one more thing. The Animacion team at the Riu was EXCELLENT. This is the activity team and seriously from 9 in the morning until midnight, these employees were doing their best to entertain the guests of the resort. From water polo to dance lessons to bingo to variety shows, they were working constantly and were the nicest people, not to mention very intelligent as most of them know FOUR languages in order to communicate with all the guests. Just amazing. Winston was our favorite and we thank you for a great time! This is a great resort and I will definitely return. I've actually been missing the Riu already! Please tip the employees, even though it states your price includes gratuity. Remember this is a very poor country and the employees work so very hard, it won't hurt anyone to tip them a few dollars throughout their stay. If you have enough money to go on a great caribbean vacation, you have enough money to tip. Go visit the Riu and have a WONDERFUL time! I'm more then happy to answer any questions you may have.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Loved the beach, would pass on the food We stayed at the Riu Taino from Feb 6- Feb 13 this month. We flew out of Minneapolis on Ryan International Airlines. Great flight, have some cash handy- they sold breakfast sandwiches or burritos for $5 each. Liquor will cost you extra also, but we just packed a few personal size shooters of rum and vodka and added them into our pop. We traveled with TransGlobal Vacations and the rep kindly directed us to our bus when we got off the plane. However, someone hadn't done their homework and we waited on the bus for 45 min for the last couple, who the other people on the bus finally told the tour guide hadn't even come with their group because of a family funeral and they were still in Minneapolis!!! That was slightly annoying, but finally, we were on the road.... went to check-in, and, apparently, our travel agent hadn't sent our confirmation voucher with us, just some E-travel documents which were not acceptable to the lady behind the counter. After some arguing, we finally got our key and nobody bothered us about the voucher during our stay, so they must have confirmed it some other way.... The beach was definitely the highlight of this trip- absolutely gorgeous, WIDE beaches with soft, powdery white sand. The water was clear blue, and you can walk along the beach for miles and miles if you choose to. Very pretty. The sound of the waves is about all you can hear on the beach, and it was very relaxing. The room was definitely acceptable. We stayed in Unit 292, in the second row of bungalows on the first level. We could see and hear the ocean from our room and it was wonderful!!!! We loved the privacy of the bungalows and were glad to have gotten a room so close to the beach. The room was always kept very clean by the maids. If you leave a few dollars, she will leave you one of the pretty towel/flower decorations. If no tip left, no towel/flower arrangements. They will stock your refrigerator with 3 beers, never any more unless you leave a special request (and probably a few bucks.) We weren't in our room much beyond sleeping and showering again in the evening before supper, so between the pop in the refrigerator, the liquor dispenser, and the 3 beers, we always had an evening drink to tide us over until we headed out again. Other thoughts: the food was not great, in our opinion. Neither my husband or I are picky eaters by any means, but we were both disappointed by the food. We never went hungry, but the flavor of the food was just not in agreement with our tastebuds, even being open-minded. I would recommend asking for a table outside. Our waiter was nice, but he was getting drunk while serving us during Friday night's supper and forgot to get our water and drinks for half an hour! We were hoping to have more opportunities to eat seafood, and after a week of hit-or-miss seafood options, we splurged on our last night and went to Captain Cooks. $55 per person, but they pick you up on a bus, take you to the oceanside restaurant- very romantic! and you are given all the alcohol you'd like (we had white wine and Presidente beer) and an AMAZING, DELICIOUS meal with salad, appetizer, and a HUGE platter of seafood- it was incredible!!! Finally satisfied our seafood cravings and would make this trip to Captain Cook's again in a heartbeat. They do not take credit cards, however, so pack an extra $110 in cash if you want to check it out. Some suggestions: 1. Take a few washcloths or a bath loofah as there will not be any washcloths supplied in your room. 2. Find a few wrist key-chains at the dollar store (as other reviews mentioned). It's an easy way to keep track of your room and safe keys. You can get a second room key for a ten dollar deposit, save your receipt, though, or you'll have trouble getting the ten bucks back when you check out. 3. Take a few insulated mugs to save on trips back up to the bar. We also filled ours up before taking off on a few strolls down the beach, and our 32 ounce mugs got us there and back with outh getting thirsty.4. If you like seafood, there will be a poolside gumbo grill-out one day during the week- delicious! But they don't have much out there for food, so make sure you get there early!5. One thing we were disappointed about was how several of the bartenders seemed to expect tips. We luckily had packed some extra cash after reading other reviews on TripAdvisor, but it gets to be really annoying to tip so often when you've already payed for all-inclusive. 6. Check out the outdoor hot tub at the Riu Palace Macao after the sun has gone down over the palm trees, but you're not quite ready to go back to your room. It's supposed to be just for palace people, but it's not guarded and was completely deserted when we went there. It was hidden back in the foliage, and SO RELAXING, we felt like we disappeared for an hour!!7. Check out the Riu Bambu- neat bars and a nice lunch area, too. Great pool.All in all, a nice vacation. We would return to Punta Cana again someday, but not to the Riu because of the food and because we want to check out some other resorts. Our friends had been at the Iberostar and said it was excellent. AVOID LTI- looks very scary!!!!! We paid $2,800 for two people, all taxes, fees included.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Our Favourite resort My husband and I just returned from our second trip to the RIU Taino, and I wanted to post another review of this resort. There have been some negative reviews of the Taino recently, and I am completely baffled as to where Leslie stayed - we didn't find any of the problems she encountered. My only response is - thanks for your comments, please feel free to STAY AWAY from our favourite resort. Okay, enough editorializing - on to the fun part - OUR TRIP! This is our second stay at the Taino, we were there for two weeks in 2004 as well. We flew USA 3000 from Detroit, flight was uneventful, food was as awful as expected. We arrived at the airport in PC, there was MUCH confusion on the plane regarding the new tourist forms, flight attendants have not been trained in the completion of the forms. But, as best we could tell - NO ONE LOOKED AT THEM - we handed them in along with our $10.00 to some women at a booth who then handed us a plastic tourist card. We boarded the bus, and were on our way. Check-in was an absolute delight, we had all of our paperwork completed, keys and cold drink in hand within minutes and we were escorted to our room. We had a first floor room in building #34, just steps from the restaurants and the lobby (thank you VERY much to Janet at Sears Travel who e-mailed a request for us!). The weather was a bit odd this year - the first 3-4 days were beautiful - straight out of the brochure. Then we had 4-5 days of very high winds and surf - most days the red flag was out - some days the flags weren't even posted - I think they were afraid they would blow away. It was still quite warm, and although it rained several times - for very short periods of time - it quickly blew out and the sun returned. The last days of our stay were back to the beautiful calm weather.My only criticism - the rooms are looking a bit dated. They do need a little modernizing - brightening up, but were spotlessly clean every day (thank you Ruth!). If I may make a request - please, please I hope they soon put in queen size beds. We're a little industrial in size, so a 3/4 and a single just won't do the job. Besides, pushing the beds together never works - guess who's always falling through the crack! ;-) Oh well, we made do. Lots of storage space - and we were on the beach before 2 p.m. I would like to make a special point to mention the staff at the RIU - this is our fourth stay at a RIU property (twice in Puerto Plata), and without exception, the staff at the RIU are the highlight of our trip. I must thank the wonderful manager at the Taino- he actually remembered us from our trip two years ago. And also the great people at the La Bamba - especially Luis Miguel, Yolanda and Octavio - and also Elpidio at the bar in the theatre - who sent someone running for a bottle of Anisette for my after-dinner drink! Thanks so much to the lovely young man at the front desk who actually took off his I want to go to RIU pin and gave it to me when I asked where I could buy one - what a sweet thing to do! In the restaurants - Francesca, Wendy and Virginia took wonderful care of us - and they were always smiling despite unbelievably long days. And Juan, who made wonderful omelettes every morning, and was so tolerant of my very limited Spanish.The food was just excellent, there was always something interesting and fun being served - from Mexican night and the awesome fajitas - incredible guacamole, Dominican night - LOVE that Cafe Diablo; roast suckling pig, shrimp, paella - so many things to choose from - and very clean and fresh. We had the 6:30 dinner seating - 8:30 is just too late for us, and enjoyed the assigned table.The beach is so beautiful - we just never get tired of spending our days out there. We love the wonderful international crowd, we met people from many countries, and as always are embarassed at how much more English they have than we have of their languages. Somehow we manage to communicate - a smile goes a long way.We took some bread down to the shore every morning and fed the fish - that was great fun - they will actually come up and nibble on your finger tips (gently!). There is one VERY large fish that lurks in the shallows in front of the resort - he quite startled me the first time I saw him - he's easily 24 long - but fortunately very docile, and also loves bread! We also went snorkeling out near the swim barriers (which seem to have been moved inwards - we were able to swim over the reef last time - this year it wasn't accessible). We took a banana out with us (it doesn't dissolve in the water while you swim), and fed the larger fish out in the deeper water - that was also fun - they were quite bold and would swim close enough to touch. They are quite discriminating - they will eat the banana, but spit out any piece of peel. We bring 30 oz. insulated mugs, we're not big drinkers, but really hate warm beer - and a small scoop of ice in the mug topped up with draft beer will stay cold for hours. Neither of us had a moment of any kind of illness, nor did we hear of anyone sick at the resort. It was constantly being cleaned, which is not an easy task - the resort was very full.Finally, I would also like to thank Iria (I'm sorry if that is misspelled) - who was so kind as to offer to deliver the school supplies we brought to a school on her way to visit her boyfriend's family in Santo Domingo. We appreciate your help - and the generosity with your free time - thank you.One other disjointed comment about the room - the showers are MARVELLOUS! There was always an abundance of hot water, and the water pressure was very strong - enough to remove the last trace of sand, sunscreen and salt - and then some! Our trip was wonderful, and we would not hesitate to return to this beautiful, friendly resort - they say welcome home as you arrive, and it's the feeling we have the whole time - that we're at home, and very welcome.  
<Date>Jan 30, 2006

<Author>kellyjelly
<Content>not a four star We stayed at the Riu Taino Jan 13 thru Jan 16. This was my first time visiting the Dominican and probably the last. I have stayed in several Riu hotels in Mexico and Jamaica and have always loved what the RIU offers, my mom even wears their staff shirt!We thought with a Riu it has to be nice, wrong. I hate when reviews drone on about the negatives so let me keep it simple. I'll start with the positives. The beach is amazing, just beautiful. The water was chilly, but I expected that for this time of year. There was always plenty of beach chairs so you could always find somewhere nice to sit. There is a flea market at the end of the beach, but if you're not a haggler don't go. I would rather pay the extra dollar and shop in peace at Carribean Street. They have basically the same merchandise. If you think you'll be warm in the pool, guess again. The pool was to cold to swim in, I only got in once, after several daquiris.The drinks were always tasty but the bartenders could care less how long it takes to serve you. They also speak very little English and do not make an attempt to let you understand them. no salt for your margherita is not in the Spanish language. My biggest problem with this resort is how indifferent the staff is about pleasing you. I'm not pampered by any means but they are very rude. The cashier in the hotel gift shop was upset with me because after asking her to sit items to purchase off to the side, she rang them up anyway. I told her i would come back in an hour with the money she rolled her eyes and gave me dirty look. She told my friend to tell what size t-shirt she was looking for so she would quit unfolding them!Upon check-in we were told the room would not be ready for an hour. We ate and cameback. We were taken to our room but the maid was still cleaning...we watched her clean for 20 more minutes! The room was very small with one double bed and two twin size beds! Do you go on vacation to sleep in a twin bed? The room was mustier than the usual smell, but fortunately I had brought an air freshener. The fridge in our room kept things luke warm with no temperature dial. It was on the second day we realized you had to wedge it up against the wall to keep it shut!Europeans seem to out number the Americans here. I'm not sure why but they seem to be the rudest here than I have ever experienced. They cut in front of you in line and bump into you as if you weren't even there. We found a wallet one day and tracked the people down ourselves. We weren't sure the hotel staff would bother returning it. They rewarded us with two Italian bottles of champagne! They were probably the nicest people we met whole time.These problems were only a fraction of the things that went on. I think this could be a great resort with a little time and effort, but it definitely needs improvement both physically and with the attitudes of customer satisfaction. I hope this has been helpful. I wish we had shopped for a better place. Maybe you would be better off at the Palace.

<Content>What a wonderful HoneyMoon! We had such a great time, it was a wonderful place and definatly something that we would go back to.Here's some of the high and low lights:1. Pools- Very clean, the pools was sweeped in the mornings, the pool bar was busy, but never full so you were always served quickly, Hector will treat you like royalty. Lots of pool games to keep you occupied or just to watch and enjoy. The towels were at a premium, so you may wanna bring your own. 2. Rooms, older, but very clean and spacious. Maids were in daily, and were very thourough. A little tip went a long way. I found the beds comfortable for a hotel, (you can't be expecting the taj mahal that you own at home). Our room was almost the farthest from the actions as you could get and it wasn't more the a minute to the action, so I don't really know why there are so many complaints on the long disatance.3. Entertainment: The best part of this resort, the animation team is wonderful, they get to know your name, who your family is and are always 'on'. There was a large variety of shows, and don't miss the caribbean street party, the best part of the week. One negative, the vendors are out in full force, so watch out if your not into that sort of thing. Most events were done in 4-5 languages so everyone knew what was going on. 4 Service: I thought it was good, some language issues, but they try really hard to get it right. Always pleasant, and smiles all day long.5: Food, between average and above average. Some meals were great, others you could do with out. Breakfast was always good plenty of choices, dinner was mostly enjoyable, lots of variety, but don't bother with the a la cartes, the're not worth the walk. Lunch was a little repeatitive, but if you bulk up on breakfast, it's not a problem.All in all I think that this was a trip of a life time. I will be going back and I think that you should give it a try too.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Taino is Fabulos! We stayed at the Riu Taino Nov 16 - Nov 23rd and it was wonderful. The Taino is centrally located among this large Riu property so all the other Riu's were easy to get to, which was a nice thing because this resort is secluded and we didn't rent a car. We received a warm welcome (and a drink) when we arrived at 4pm and were given a nice room too. The staff always had a smile and a hello whenever they saw you. The beach was beautiful and long and the water was wavy and warm. The crowd was a little older than I expected, but we found everyone was friendly. The food was great at Taino buffet, with a large variety of dishes to choose from. We were disappointed with dinner at the Steak House (and we are not that picky). If you want to see how the Dominican people really live, we highly recommend that you take the Safari excursion, where you can visit a family's house and farm, stop at a school (bring school supplies from home to give to the kids because the people are very poor and the government does not supply those items) and even stop at a ranch to enjoy a beachside lunch, horseback riding or swimming. We would recommend this hotel to our friends as a great place to get away from the hustle of city life and be treated like royalty. Thanks Taino!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A cruise ship that never leaves the beach and has free drinks! RIU TAINO IS WONDERFUL.Obnoxious Americans Beware - please stay away from this place if you are a demanding, hard to please American. PLEASE DON'T MESS THIS UP FOR THE REST OF US.Riu Taino is the nicest place FOR THE MONEY, I've ever stayed. It's like a cruise ship that stays on a beautiful beach all the time, has unlimited drinks, a monster swimming pool and a crew that are a non-stop party.As far as I can tell Riu Taino is predominantly Europian upper working class (Spain, France and Germany). THERE ARE VERY FEW ENGLISH SPEAKING PEOPLE. The staff speaks enough to get you by but if this frustrates you, then stay somewhere else.The Beach is gorgious, wide and long. It is about 70 percent topless and almost bottomless. (This does not bother me but the 400 pound German man in a Speedo was a little much.)No locals bother you. It is on the windward side so it is a little rougher than say the Bahamas.The pool is perfect. It's large and very close to the beach. A lot of other resorts have the pool back away from the beach. At Taino you step over the wall and you are there. At about 11AM pool game start and continue to about 5PM. They are a blast to watch but you have plenty of room to stay out of the action. No shortage of drinks at the swim up bar.The food and drinks are wonderful, constant and plentiful. We did not get sick. Only drinking water is used for food prep and ice. We ate salad everyday. Bottle water is always available. You may experience a little stomach upset if you have are weak stomached. We experienced a little discomfort but we attributed it to the change in the amount we ate and the change in cooking style and food type. We always carry medications in case when we travel out of the country. We did not need them at Riu.The staff at Riu Taino is well, remarkable at the least you can say. They are all eager to please and work very hard. I believe most of them work from sun up to 1AM and then do it all again, with a smile. The Animation Staff (the Entertainment group) are a total blast and everyone is magnetized to them.The rooms are spacious and modern with an inroom bar and refridge, well stocked. A/C works very well. Maid service is excellent.DR is a very poor country and the staff gets paid very little. Unlike most others, we were careful to tip everyone a little something. You can get 3000 pecos for $100. We normally tipped a 30 pecos bill to the bartender several times a day, which will get you a better brand and makes you a friend. The servers about 50 to 100 a night. The maid 150 a day, the in room bar guys about 50 a day. We even tipped the pool guys and the grounds keepers a little because our little tips would go a long ways with there families. Most live an hour away in Higuey and travel by bus. We like to see some of the little people behind the scenes get something and when you tip them you will be able to tell it does not happen very often. You can walk to any of the Riu Resorts and eat, do a show and use the facilities. There are street dances and shows and indoor shows everynight.Notes: Try to fly into Punta Cana Airport. Also, there is a hospital close by and a 24 hour / 7 day doctors office, on site, if you need help.Once again, you can spend more money and stay at a newer, larger resort with bigger shows. But for the money Riu Taino is not a 5 it's a 10.Mark Curtiss, Lexington SC USA

And we ate everything from salads to fruit. But let's start with the room. It is allright but nothing nice, it does need renovation. We liked the fact that they were individual buildings, we don't like those huge hotels where you need elevators to your room. (The Naiboa was like that) Not the best thing to have a double and a single when you are a couple and the furniture is old wicker, ugly curtains, old bathroom. But everything functioned well and it did not stink. And we did not stay there much so this did not ruin anything for us although was definetely not 5 star. The minibar was filled about every 3rd to 4th day and we only ran out of water a couple of times so we called the reception and it was taken care of, just don't wait till the evening to do that or you will have to wait till the next day. The maid cleaned every day, service was pretty standard. The hotel was generally clean, public bathrooms were being cleaned constantly, I could not go to one without seeing someone cleaning. The reception and all the other buildings also look old, not such a pleasant athmosphere especially in the restaurant and theather, the Bambu is a whole lot nicer. We always ate outside and went to the Bambu for the night shows so therefore it did not bother us but really, it was not that pretty and again, not 5 star, or maybe it was one time but they need to renovate and bring this place more up to date. Again, it did not ruin our time but that is the honest truth. The pool area is not that big but nice and very close to the beach unlike at the Bambu which is bigger but more distant from the beach. The beauty of having a variety, we really enjoyed that. The pool wasn't that clean time to time but then a day or 2 later we noticed they had cleaned it. We did not hang out much there during the day so I can't report much about fighting for chairs but we noticed they were going fast in the morning. The beach was nice, loved all the Palmtrees, especially at the Bambu it was great, the Taino had less at the beach for shades and so did the Palace. The sand was nice and soft and you could walk forever but the water itself was not as nice as per say in Cuba just because it was windier here so it stirred up the sand. But Cuba lacked the Palmtrees and food wasn't that good there. Snorkelling was a disappointment, the coral is mainly dead here, you do see some fish etc but we thought it was going to be better after reading the reviews here. We rented a car and drove to Bayahibe to the caribbean side and the water there was beautiful along with snorkelling. If you take excursions to Catalina or Saona you will bee in the Caribbean. One thing that was really-really bad were the cocktails. Pina coladas and such:(((( Even if we asked them to blend it with ice it was not slushy since they only blended it for a bit so it was just liquid with ice cubes and the taste was not that good either. Bananamamas were tasty but again, not slushy. So we did not drink much and never used the isolated cups we always bring to AI places and this was quite a let down. We are not boozers but would have liked to enjoy frozen drinks like we did in Cuba and Mexico. Food: we ate breakfast and dinner at the main restaurant outside, we much preffered outside. Lunch always at the Bambu, for change of place and also it was slightly better. Someone mentioned the paellas at the Pizzeria by the scubashop so we checked it out and have to say it was more like spanish rice then paella. They served real paellas couple of times at the Bambu snack bar for lunch and when they had a beach BBQ lunch once a week there and it was awesome!!! The snackbar at the Taino did not have enough variety, Bambu had some more. Breakfast was pretty good, lots of variety, I liked the cinnamon covered croissants. It was the same every day though which is expected I guess. We loved the pizza, reminded me back home in Europe, I don't like the american pizzas at all, and here the veggies had actual taste and the dough was not sweet, anyway, loved it. True about desserts, they were awesome and lot of them, very very good so if you like desserts you will be satisfied. The menu was repetitive but this is expected at any AI resort, lots of variety though and we did not think it was blend, everything had a flavour. The mexican night was great, we really missed having chips and salsa with guacamole on a daily basis like in Mexico so we wished they would have had them as snacks during the day. We also missed more grilled food like shrimp, calamar and fish, they did have them but not grilled. The fruits however were awesome!!! We read earlier here someone suggesting not to eat them, that would be a huge mistake since they are delicious!!!! Sweet pineapples, mangos, papayas, passion fruit, grapefruit etc, all very good, maybe except for the watermelon. So all in all the food was good but not excellent, we did not look forward to meals like some other places we have been to. A'la cartes, well really nothing great but we did not care too much and only went once to each and never thought about them again.Service was pretty good everywhere at the resort and the staff was friendly. Nightshows are not that great and gets pretty repetitive since most of them are dance shows with some silly animation stuff, definetly not 5 star quality and not very professional and dancers need new outfits. We did go to the Bambu almost every night though since there is not much else to do and we prefered over there since it was outside. Caribbean street party was Ok but after the reviews here we thought it was going to be something real special. Taking the catamaran out was fun but it gets tricky sometimes when there is not much wind. My husband got his open water scuba certificate there and he enjoyed it although visibility was so much better down south at the caribbean side. Shopping was good just off the resort next to Iberostar, don't forget to bargain though. We did go to Bavaro to look around once and the vendors there are a lot more agressive so we sticked to this place, they had the same stuff. I would suggest not touching the dogs laying around, I saw one while getting sick, not a pretty site. Sunqest rep Julie was not very nice, we asked her about some info on Bayahibe and renting a car and she was not willing to answer questions, just kept repeating how they don't recommend it. I used to work as a tourguide for years so I know they rely on the comission they get from selling their trips but still she could have been more informative and polite especially since I told her I used to do the same before. At the end I just asked her if she is driving which seemed to get her face red all around. We did go to check out the Palladium, we walked at the beach (quite the distance but we were on a mission) and then jumped on the little train to see all the Palladium hotels. It is beautiful and I believe it would have been great there too, if not even better then at the Taino. Everything seemed new there and their beach was nice too. The grounds were more manicured, ours seemed more wild and natural which I think we preferred. Bavaro Princess looked great too, the beach at the LTI stinked, not nice. Bahia Principe next door to Bambu had some seaweeds and less Palmtrees, Iberostar on the other side seemed nice. The airport is the coolest I have ever seen, especially when we arrived we were impressed. Service ok, security not intimidating and at check-in they did not care much about weight either. So all in all it was a great vacation and I would go back to the Dominican sometime down the road. If it had to be the Riu we would still gladly go back but I feel we paid too much for what we got since it is not a 5 star hotel, more like 4 so it should be a bit cheaper. And no, I am not talking canadian standards, I did not expect that down there. It isn't really about the stars anyway, I just feel we did not get the value for our money. So look out for deals and have fun!!!!!

<Content>lots of info Just got back, March 8/2005. What an amazing beach, no words can explain, just really really great and lots of fun. Snorkel as much as you can, its amazing. We Parasailed, but for 85$ a person its an individual thing. Overall, the Rui Taino hotel is probably a 4 star, but the staff is a 6 star, the service is a 6 star, the food is a 6 star, but the age of the hotel hurts its ratings, if you cant enjoy this place, this beach and what you can do outside the resort than dont go to the DR, its not for you. <Rating>4	-1	-1	-1	-1	-1	-1	-1	

<Author>RhodyTraveller
<Content>Great Experience at Riu Taino Our family (2 adults, two teenagers) stayed at the Riu Taino February 18-25, 2005. We had a wonderful time and would go back. Our only prior experience in Punta Cana was at the Barcelo Palace, and we would rate the two as roughly equivalent, with the Riu Taino having the edge for liveliness and staff friendliness, and the Barcelo having slightly better accommodations and food. We arrived at the Riu Taino on a Friday mid-afternoon. Since we did not take a charter, we arrived at the hotel by taxi (arranged in advance through Coco Tours, the local agent of TNT Tours) not tour bus, so there was no crowd at check in. We had scoped out the room locations in advance, and had e-mailed the hotel prior to arrival for a room closer to the beach. The hotel had e-mailed us back, indicating that they could not guarantee location, since it was their busy season. We initially were assigned to a room at the back of the property (near the Naiboa), but after some persistent (but nice) urging, the reception staff located rooms opening up the next day closer to the beach. The reception staff, particularly Rossy, was very helpful and attentive, and spoke English very well. We moved the next day, and were very happy with the location. We had two rooms on the second floor, which worked out well since our teenagers were right next to us.  We liked the bungalow set up of the Riu Taino, rather than large buildings like some other hotels. Our one complaint about the rooms (hopefully the Riu management reads these reviews) is that they really need updating, particularly as to curtains and bedding. We are more interested in the beach, pool, restaurants, etc., and did not spend much time in the room, so this was not a big deal to us. The cleaning staff deserves kudos for dealing with the mess left each day by two teenage girls. We made sure to leave a few dollars each day as our way of thanking the cleaning staff. The restaurants were satisfactory, but nothing special. We thought the food was a touch better at the Barcelo Palace, although we certainly never went hungry. We really liked the fact that food was available almost any time of day (until about mid night). When the main dining room is closed, you can get hot snacks, fruit, coffee, soda, etc. at the pizza restaurant on Caribbean Street or at the main bar area near the pool. There are two seatings, since the main restaurant is not large enough to accommodate everyone. We were assigned to the 8:30 seating, which we initially thought we would not like, but didn't try to change and actually ended up liking the late dinner (we would get a late afternoon snack at the bar to hold us over). We exercised the same caution with buffet food as we would in the U.S. We stuck to the hot food, fruits, pizza and breads, and stayed away from the salad bars and cold food. (The salad bar and cold food looked fine, just our self-imposed caution.) We did not experience or hear anyone else complain about any of the illness problems that have garnered a lot of attention. The hotel was extremely clean, and they seemed to go out of their way to keep it that way. We didn't notice a flying or walking bug the whole time. The food definitely reflected the European clientele, with a number of hot dishes with a Germanic tone to them. We would have liked to see more grilled to order fish and chicken, rather than grilled foods prepared in advance and then set out in pans. There was plenty of red meats, but we are not heavy meat eaters, so we can't attest to the quality. The clientele definitely was heavily European, with a large percentage of Germans, some French, and a variety of others (Italy, Eastern Europe, etc.). There was a heavy contingent of wild and crazy English speaking Canadians (is there any other type?), but just a few Americans. Contrary to some reports, the Germans were just fine, but somewhat more reserved, which could be misinterpreted as rude. Our casual observation was, nonetheless, the closer you got to the buffet, the more likely you were to have a close encounter with a German senior citizen coming back for more.  The Europeans smoke incessantly, which we also observed at the Barcelo Palace. It was shocking to see mid-teen Europeans chain smoking in front of their parents. The ventilation was good everywhere except the disco and the bar off the lobby, so this was not a huge problem. The animacion staff, particularly Rigo, Rosa, Jimy and their boss (never did get his name) were great. For us, this was the key difference which likely will cause us to return to the Riu Taino over the Barcelo Palace. The pool area was a buzz of activity, and the staff extremely energetic and friendly. I never got the feeling that anyone was looking for a tip, although we handed out plenty of tips just before we left to thank the animacion staff for making our trip so great. The beach is beautiful, although less intimate than the Barcelo Palace. We had a particularly windy week, so we ended up spending more time at the pool than we had anticipated. The pool chairs were reserved early (by 8 a.m. they were gone), but that was not a problem for us since I got up early each morning for a run on the beach. For you runners out there, the beach is more suited to running than at the Barcelo Palace, since it is wider with more of a water line (so you don't have to run on heavy sand). Having run a half-hour or so in each direction, I can attest that the Riu Taino has the best beach in sight.  We did not spend much time at the other Riu hotels. The Riu Palace looked beautiful, but was too fancy for our tastes (we go away to dress down, not dress up). The Riu Bambu was much newer, but we liked the location of the Riu Taino, which was closer to the beach and Caribbean street. We were much more comfortable letting our teenagers stay out late at the disco on Caribbean street since it was just minutes from the Riu Taino, but farther from the Riu Bambu. Our only complaint, if you call it that, is that the Riu needs to exercise closer control over the independent vendors they allow on the property. We had a bad experience with the hairdresser (for braiding) on Caribbean Street, which has a booth at the pool. We were willing to pay more than the braiding at the market down the beach, for the convenience of having it done at the pool. The braiding was not the way my 14 year old daughter had described (probably a language problem), but when we asked them to correct it, they wanted to charge us another $20. The money was insignificant, but we objected to paying more just to get it right. The owner of the hair salon was extremely aggressive, going to the extent of trying to get the manager of the Riu Taino to force us to pay. Fortunately, the manager, a very nice guy from Spain, backed us up 100%.  Also, the hotel allows outside vendors into the hotel lobby once a week to show their wares, mostly jewelry, cigars, paintings and tee shirts. This is fine with us, but we felt uncomfortable since the vendors were aggressive in trying to get us to buy. This is fine when this happens at the beach market, but not on the hotel property. These minor complaints, however, hardly detracted from our overall experience. We would rate the Riu Taino a solid 4+ star (by Punta Cana standards), and it would be a 5 star with a little cosmetic updating. We will be back for sure. BW from Rhode Island.  
<Date>Feb 26, 2005

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Wonderful vacation, beautiful beach My husband and I just returned from a very relaxing vacation in the DR. We stayed at the Riu Taino Feb. 8 - 13. We have been to other all-inclusives and this was the best yet. We were greated with a fruity coctail. Check-in took no time at all, about 2 mins. Enough time to tell us about the towel cards, safe, mini bar, and bottled water in the room. We were taken to our room, changed clothes and headed to the beach. It was windy a few of the days we were there, but it kept you from sweating in the sun. It was easy to move from the shade of the palm trees to the sun on the beach by just moving your chair a couple feet. That was great for us since I was out for a tan and my husband has more difficuty without burning. We still sat together without any problems. We thought the food was good. We went to both resturaunts, which were also good, but enjoyed the selection at the buffet. The main dishes changed evey night. The french toast was wonderful at breakfast. My husband had bowel problems with some nausea for about 4 hours one evening, but he blamed in on the not quite fully cooked piece of sausage he had for breakfast that morning. The symptoms were gone the next day so he was probably right. I didn't have the sausage or any type of problems while we were there. I also didn't hear or see anyone else with problems. We ventured over to the Bambu and thought the lunch was better at the Tanio although another couple thought the Melao was better (it's a more French dominated, and more women topless on the beach) We didn't get there to eat, but we walked to all of them, including the Palace. We sat on the beach in front of the Palace one day and used there pool a couple times to cool off even though your not suppose to if your not staying there. They have to wear wrist bands. No one that I could see checked for them and if they noticed they didn't care or say anything. I'm sure they would if you tried to eat or drink there. Eveyone around the pool, as my husband said, was on life support. It was very quiet, no one was walking around or using the pool, except us. Our pool was pretty active. I got up early, around 7:30 as opposed to closer to 9:00, a couple days and saw that a few of the pool chairs were being saved but most hadn't. My question for these people on a mission to have a pool side seat is Why not save some money and go someplace not on the beach if you are so set on being by a pool all day? You can do that at the Holiday Inn's indoor pool at home. We were on the beach everyday, the sand was soft and not at all hot on your feet. I brought a large mug with a lid. We filled it every morning at breakfast with whatever we wanted to drink until lunch. The water and ice are fine to consume in the bar and resturants. I love to chew ice while lying in the sun and I did plenty of it there and didn't have any problems. Our plane didn't leave until 4pm and the bus didn't pick us up until 1pm.(You really do need about 2-3 hours to get to the airport and through the bagage check line, they search EVERY bag). Check out is at noon, I asked if we could have a late check out, not yet knowing what time the bus was coming, and they said we could stay in our room until 2:30. They actually thought that we didn't understand when we came to check out at 1:00 and we explained that our bus was making us leave. We were surprise at how fast check out was if that's what you'd call it. We gave them the keys and towel cards and they said OK, it looks like everything is in order. We hope you had a good time. That was it, no papers, signatures, or extra bills. The staff are wonderful and the bar tenders recognize you and remember what you usually drink. They spoke some English, German, and French that we could understand, probably other languages that we didn't. Not all fluently, but enough to make you feel like you could communicate what you wanted. I had read all of the reviews before going. When we booked our vacation the Riu Taino was ranked #7. Then this Norvirus thing started and it dropped to around #11. We had the chance to change hotels through United Vacations because of illness going around. I almost did except the resort that we could change to still wasn't ranked as high as Taino even though it was also 5 star. I'm glad we didn't. Whatever was going around must be gone because we did everything but drink the tap water and brought along some hand sanitizer.I think your vacation is what you make of it. If you go there looking for the bad things you'll find something wrong anywhere you go. If you go looking to enjoy a relaxing vacation, not having to cook, clean, go to work, or be in the cold weather you will have a wonderful time.

<Content>Don't go to this so-called five star resort My wife and I were at the Taino from January 7, 2005 through Januaray 14, 2005. To make the double bed, they covered the mattress with a twin sheet which could not be tucked in. Then they put another twin sheet as a top sheet but this was tucked in at the bottom and therefore came up only to chest height. That left you with a light cover. When you rolled over at night, the bottom sheet bunched up and you were left lying on a bare mattress and could only wonder how many others had done the same and then all the other possibilities of what could be in the mattress come to mind. Food was adequate but very repititious. Not much variety at the snack bar. Areas were generally well kept and staff were somewhat friendly. Beach area was small - three or four rows of chairs and you were in the ocean. We were forced to be at the pool early to get a couple of chairs. While you can't blame the resort, the weather was OK except for the constant heavy wind which forced you to use the chairs as a protection from the cool wind coming off the water. On our last night, someone got into our room while we were having supper - didn't get anything as we had keys to the safe with us and left nothing of any value out - but it is somehwat unnerving to find that this can so easily happen. We certainly won't go back to the DR and will only use the RIU chain again because of the free week mentioned early which has to be taken at the same chain.

If you want it, offer them about 1/3rd of what they're asking and its yours. We didn't get there this time though.My wife and I both got very sick. I am still having stomach problems 11 days after our return. I became sick on January 5 and on January 15 (after our return home). I returned to normal on January 6, but took several days to return to normal after the 15th vomiting episode. I had serious chills and fever. My wife started her diarrhea on January 6th. I took her to the clinic on Caribbean Street on the moning of the 8th and received an almost immediate ambulance ride to the Bavaro Hospital. The emergence room doctor called it travelers' diarrhea!!!? Whatever, she was very ill early in the morning and briefly passed-out. After getting back to the resort and having a liquid lunch, it resulted in a violent vomiting episode. It's amusing now, but she did feel better after that!! The hospital gave her four medications. I was impressed with the sincerity and concern expressed by all of the medical personnel. The Cuyahoga County (Cleveland) Health Board is doing an investigation as many people became ill at this resort. I will be trying another Caribbean destination.

<Author>redd
<Content>Amazing Beach Holiday Riu Taino- 15 nights. Dec.8-Dec 23/04 My husband and myself- early 40鈥檚, have been to Puerto Plata, Sosua and Cabarete on the North Coast as well as Samana and Las Galeras on previous trips to the DR and decided it was time to check our Punta Cana. We flew via Air Transat direct from Edmonton, Alberta landing at the Punta Cana airport after 6.5 hours at 6:00pm on a Wednesday. (The flight back was 7.5 hours). We had ample room on the flight down due to the Malaria scare and cancellations. The flight back however, was full and cramped; thankfully we each had an aisle seat so legs could be stretched out. We were the only two from our flight that were going to the Riu resorts so we had the luxury of being transported via Coco tours by van. We arrived after 30 min to the Taino. The reception was welcoming and we were processed quickly. We found any request we had quickly responded to: i.e. a t.v remote needed and 5 min later delivered to our room or if more water or beer was needed for our mini-fridge鈥?done! Awesome service and management showed real concern about any query we had. Internet was available in the lobby area for 5US/20minutes.Rooms:The rooms were adequate, we tried out two while we were there and actually preferred the area farther back since it was quieter. We stayed in bungalow 591 for the first week. It was ground level and in a very lush area. The room had a double and two twin beds, mini-safe, mini-fridge stocked with beer (not Presidente beer but Quisqueya, and pop), liquor dispenser of brandy, amber  white rum and vodka. The furniture was wicker, the AC worked well as did the ceiling fan. The terrace was large but it was too hot and humid to spend any amount of time on it. They sprayed for mosquitoes while we were there so no worries about being surrounded by the lovely vegetation. We had a banana tree, complete with a stalk of bananas outside our terrace. We had about a 5-10 minute walk to the restaurant-beach area. Since we were there for 15 nights we thought a change of view would be nice, so after a week we asked to change to a room closer to the beach. No problem, they moved us to 043 second floor ocean view. It was a great location to the beach, but a smaller room and of course nosier since we were much closer to all the action. It had most of the same amenities as the first room, except only a double and one twin bed and the mini-fridge was in the closet. The balcony was nice since you got more of a breeze being on the second floor. So whichever room you do get there are pros and cons to each. Bars:The Taino鈥檚 lobby/beach bar had the best service. It was opened until 2 am. The Bambu had a 24 hr bar that we checked out a couple of evenings and it was fun but the service was not as a good. We checked out most of the bars (what else do you do with 15 nights) and the Taino seemed to be where a lot of people ended up. The disco was not really happening or if it was we missed that night. Restaurants:The buffet restaurant was very well laid out. There were two dinner seatings, 6:30 and 8:30. You were given the same numbered table every night. This avoided having to grab a table and fight lineups etc. that we have experienced at other resorts. The hot food was hot and the cold food cold. There were many choices available. I avoided the raw salads but my husband ate them without any complaints. We tried the steakhouse and that was not great. Although many people were happy with the mixed grill, we had ordered the steak and we found it to be thin and tough. We didn鈥檛 try the Mediterranean. Breakfasts were very good and we also enjoyed lunches at the Pizzeria and lobby/beach bar. Overall, we liked the food.Weather, Bugs, Illness:The weather was awesome the entire time with only one day of solid rain. It was +30C the entire time with cool breezes off the ocean. The flags were green or yellow so ocean sports and swimming were entirely possible and enjoyable. Mosquitoes were few; I think we saw two or three the entire time. I did take the malaria prophylaxis, Novo Chloroquine (2x250mg tablets once a week for 7 weeks total). My husband did not bother. I didn鈥檛 get any mosquito bites; however, I did get about 8 odd burn-like marks on one of my legs, with two that actually blistered. Not sure what caused them, they didn鈥檛 look like bites, could I have rubbed against a poisonous plant?? No idea. I bought some antibiotic cream from the local Pharmacia and it seemed to help. They are almost healed now that I am home, but they may scar. My husband did not get a single bite. Geesh!I suffered some stomach upset after taking my pill but nothing major. I had no problems with the food or water. My husband had some diarrhea but I am sure the 20 beer a day had nothing to do with it. Ha! However, many people at the resort did suffer a day or two of illness. It was hot and very easy to become dehydrated so beware and drink lots of water. The resort management were very concerned with the number of people complaining of illness and changed their water suppliers while we were there. One gentleman we spoke to has been coming to this resort for the past six years and this was the first time he had any problems with illness. People:When we first arrived the majority of people were Germans, Swiss, and French etc. We found that most people were very friendly if you attempted conversation (many people spoke some English or just smiled and nodded as we raised our glasses to them). We met a couple of Americans and a Welsh family the second night there. And after a week it was the Canadian invasion, ha! So speaking English was not a problem and my husband who speaks Polish even met 2 couples from Poland (they spoke English as well) that were just a blast to hang out with. We also met a couple of fellows from Argentina and a Spanish couple. The one major difference with being in Punta Cana compared to Puerto Plata (we鈥檝e spent a month on the north coast on previous trips) is that you really don鈥檛 get much of a local feel. Most of the locals travel by bus an hour or so to get to work at the Rius, or stay at the resort during their work schedule. (i.e. the Animation team stays in residences near the Naiboa) Pool and Beach:We spent most of our days on the marvellous beach- he in the sun and me in the shade of a palm tree, Fantastic, you walk into the ocean on powdery beige sand and the water was clear. The beach seemed endless as it was long and wide. There was never a problem getting a lounger on the beach, no saving needed. However, the pool was a different story, saving loungers started at around 7 am. We found it too hot-no breeze at all by the pool so this was not even a concern for us. The most entertaining pool was at the Bambu, it had the biggest pool bar as well as lively contests to watch. The Bambu pool was beautiful and had a large bar above the swim-up bar that was nicely shaded and allowed for a cooler place to watch the fun. The Tainos pool was nice as well but its swim-up bar was smaller but well attended.Entertainment:The animation team works hard and they were very entertaining, especially watching poor hapless tourists such as ourselves- who got talked into taking part in their skits and contests.We won a bottle of rum each for our participation. It was a good laugh.Shopping:Here is where we felt somewhat frustrated, the prices were high because there is little competition and much of the merchandise is repetitive. There was either Carribean street where bartering was not needed or you could walk down the beach to the huts and barter for your merchandise. (better deals that way) The closet town of Higuey is an hour away by taxi, and hour and half by bus. So if you go to Punta Cana it鈥檚 for the Beach not the shopping.Summary: We enjoyed this vacation although 15 days was a tad long, we aren鈥檛 ones to lay around lounging all day but we did start to get the hang of it. We enjoyed the North Coast because there was more to do but Punta Cana definitely has better beaches. We did not do excursions on this trip as we have done plenty in the past.

StudySpanish. A complete tutorial for FREE (grammar and pronunciation). I'm half way through the suggested on-line lessons and enjoying every minute of it!Bring insulated water bottles to keep hydrated during long walks on the beach. There's some self serve water and ice at the La Bamba (along with juices, soft drink, ice tea, etc). We filled these up and were set for hours.Don't miss the beach BBQ (grilled meats and great sangria), Steakhouse (awesome steak and service to boot!), a shot of mama juana with coffee after dinner, and beautiful pictures taken by photographers throughout the day ($7 each), for memories that will last a lifetime.Would we go back? <Author>kappyfisher
<Content>Great place but beware of thieves My girlfriend and I just returned from 7 days in Punta Cana. I am 48 and she is 35 and we were looking for a nice beach vacation after enjoying the Iberostar Pairaiso Del Mar in Playa Del Carmen last October. We originally booked the Riu Naiboa, but were not happy with the property when we arrived. The food seemed low end and we couldn't find a room to our liking after repeated attempts. The Naiboa is pretty far off the beach as well. We knew it was a step down when we booked it but didn't expect to be as disappointed as we were upon arrival. We paid an extra $200 to move to the Taino and it was money well spent. We ended up with a 4 unit bungalow fairly close to the beach as well as the pool and the room was much better than at the Naiboa. The food was noticeably better as well. We were on the 2nd floor of the bungalow and on the 3rd night, we did have someone scale the balconey and enter our room through the sliding doors while we were at dinner. Our valuables were in the safe thankfully, and so our losses only amounted to clothing worth about $500. Another couple we ran into was not so fortnuate. They were on the first floor in a different unit and had locked all the doors, but were still robbed. They had just arrived and had not put their valuables in the safe so they lost everyting, including their passports. They had to make a 6 hour round trip to Santa Domingo to get them replaced. RIU did a pretty good job accomodating both of us and offered us 4 nights free on our next Caribbean trip and dinner at the higher end Riu Palance as compensation. Plus we got a free excursion to the local police department which was quite an experience. It looks like our Apple travel insurance will reimburse us for our loss so overall, it is not a huge negative. But based on our experience and that of this other couple, I would recommend that you be extremely careful about securing your items while in Punta Cana. At first, we didn't think PC was as nice as our October Playa vacation. But by the end, we both decided we would come back to PC before Playa. The beach is slightly better and we just had more fun. The Taino Animation staff were friendly, fun loving and very talented with their dancing and fluency in 4 different languages. We particularly enjoyed the twice daily dance lessons and the nightly shows which incorporated the merenge and salsa dances that we learned.Americans and the english language were definitely in the minority here. Mainly Germans and Spanish and Canadians. We liked this aspect as it truly gave an international feel to the vacation and we were still able to meet people and make friends.Regarding getting sick, I followed the advice of an earlier review and took one half of a Pepto tablet each morning and night and I did not get sick. My friend did not take the Pepto and she did have one bout of diahhria the night before we left. We also brought our own bottled water as we did not trust the gallon jug of water that they provided each day.Also, if you want to use the workout facilities, make sure you bring tennis shoes as they will not let you work out without them.Overall, the Taino was just right for us. The Naiboa was too low end and while the Palace would have been nice for the better food and more luxurious setting , we saw many Palace people enjoying the more relaxed and fun atmosphere of the Taino.We will be back to the Taino....probably soon given our 4 free night voucher that we earned!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>This must be paradise... In September we have been on a 2-week holiday in Riu Taino and it was great! I visited this website very regularly and I can assure you, only believe the positive evaluations? We first had an overbooking (travel agency's fault?), but after 2 days in the Barcelo Bavaro Palace, we were finally able to go to Riu Taino. Barcelo Palace is a lot more expensive and should be much better, but we were very very very happy to have made the change to the Taino. The rooms are very nice, located in beautiful gardens, clean, cool (has the inventor of airconditioning already won a Nobelprice?),? The beds were rather small, but hey, you aren't there to sleep all day, are you? The pool was great. There were always more than enough sunbeds and there is a great swim-up bar. If you are thirsty you'll certainly get a drink. Maybe it'll be something different than what you asked for, but that makes it more exiting. You get to know a lot of new drinks (like Mamajuana?)! The main restaurant is wonderful! You want to eat pizza, fries, chicken,? every day? No problem! But if you want to put some variation in your menu, you'll enjoy the buffets. We loved the food. It's well prepared, nicely presented, there's more than enough (although some Germans thought there wasn't? Taking 2 or 3 plates at the time?), the Mexican-evenings with Tacos and Chili con carne were superbe,? Wonderful! We also went to the Mediterannea Restaurant, but liked the normal buffet more. The Steakhouse on the other hand was very good. We tried the grilled plate and it's a recommendation! We didn't got sick at all!!! Just make sure you use the gallon of water in your room to brush your teeth and you'll be fine. The hotel-staff is incredible. Whenever and where ever you meet them, there is always a big smile and a friendly Hola. Jardineros, piscineros, waiters, bartenders, the people at the reception,? What a difference to other hotels we have been too! And if you prefer an active holiday, you can join in to an activity from the Animation-team every 30 minutes. And, believe me, these guys are completely loco! If you're planning a visit, try to locate 'Romeo' and 'Moreno DiCaprio'. As crazy as can be, but great fun! The staff of these hotels doesn't earn a lot, so when you give them a tip, they really appreciate it. We left $1 on our bed every morning and we gave occasional tips to other people, like the gardners? When you hear a strange noice in one of the gardens and you see coconuts falling out of a tree. Look up, there is probable a 'jardinero' in the tree. They even offer you fresh coconuts on the spot. They take their machete (very big and sharp knife) and prepare it on demand! We gave them a tip every time they did something like this? One last good advice : take a good spray against mosquitos! And don't forget some lotion to put on mosquito-stings? Don't ask me how these little monsters did it, but I stopped counting on 45 mosquito-stings. And they do itch! If you need to, you can finds sprays and lotions in the Caribbean Street. We did only two excursions... We went to visit the sigar-factory of Don Lucas (a Belgian guy) and we did the 3-in-1 excursion. On one day you go by bus, by boat, by airplane, by... We saw amazing things, drank cubalibre all day, got a nice tan, saw wonderful underwater-life,... One good advice : Do not buy the videotape they make on that trip. Our guide assured us that it was good quality, but it's crap! Better shoot your own pictures and take your own camera. Anything will be better than the so-called-professional cameraguy does... Our general rating? Riu Taino is an absolute 5*-place and we loved it!
