<Content>I want to go back! We stayed a week at the Taino and had a blast! The staff was wonderful, the room was clean, the whole experience was great. It's not always just the surroundings that make the trip. We three couples had so much fun, it's impossible to explain. The room size was fine because who wants to spent a lot of time in the room? The whole idea of going to someplace warm in the winter is not to sit inside your room. It can't get better than sitting under palm trees near the ocean with warm breezes, and that sound of waves washing up on shore. Especially when you know you just got 12 inches of snow back home! There were new foods for us to experience. So we tasted them. Liked some of the stuff and didn't like some of it. But that's OK. The buffet had some of the same foods at night, but it seemed there was always a theme entree. Mexican night one night, even beef and ham. So you don't have to try everything the first night you're there. I liked the fried cheese at breakfast. Reminded me a little of cheese curds. (I am a Wisconsin girl.) We went snorkeling with the sharks, parasailing, and some of us even saw a whale! You wont regret this vacation. Just don't get hung up on no washcloths in the room, or what other people do. So some women are topless, and larger men wear speedos. Get over that and enjoy the time away from work and the responsibilities of life. This is your vacation. Make it worth while. When you get back home you may have to shovel snow, and you'll surely have to go back to work. So go to the Riu. All the places looked wonderful. We might try the Bambu next time. And if you happen to see Alexis at the bar say hi for me!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>The Riu Taino was great Our one week stay at the Riu Taino was fantastic. There were five of us in total, and it was our first vacation. We found the food to be good. The breakfast was amazing......bacon, sausage, sugar donuts, and best of all the french toast croisants....mmm. The lunch was not very good...I had fries every single day. It consisted of hamburgers, hot dogs, pizza and mostly leftovers from the previous night's dinner. For dinner there was a huge selection of food at the buffet. They had different theme nights all the time. I am a very picky eater and I was perfectly fine. Most importantly, none of us got sick. The good thing about the buffet restaraunt is that you pick your table the first night, and that's your table for the whole week. We enjoyed the buffet so we didnt even bother trying the other restaraunts. My parents later went to the Iberostar Bavaro for their anniversary, and my mom got REALLY sick. The staff was very very friendly, the nightly entertainment was a little amateur, but it kept you entertained. The bingo at night was fun. Everyday they had activities...water polo...water aerobics...and sometimes even competitions between the Canadians, Americans, Germans etc...which was always fun....GO CANADA! If you don't like loud music, then dont stay at the pool. At the pool, you were always fighting for a spot. We would go put our towels down before we went to eat breakfast, I suggest you do the same. The towels were a little rough, but hey, you were given towels. The beach was great, the sand and water was gorgeous....however the water was a little choppy, and for someone who can't swim, it kind of scared me a little! There was usually a nice breeze at the beach. A downside to the beach is that you can't get any huts, there is no escaping the sunlight. Last but not least the rooms....they were a little far from the pool and restaraunts but I enjoyed the walk. They were kept very clean...however I noticed that the flowers the maids put on the counters and such had lots of little bugs coming from them, so we always threw them away immediately. But we did not find anything disgusting...so we were pleased. We found the Riu Taino to be absolutely fantastic, and we'll be at the Riu Caribe in Cancun, Mexico in about a week :) I'll keep you posted on that too. Well there you go, that's my review....if you're planning a vacation that consists of sitting back and relaxing, the Taino is a good place to go!!!

<Content>A Tropical Paradise This place was fantastic. A virtual tropical paradise. More than I would have expected. We (my husband, and twin 18 year old daughters) just spent a week there. The little gym could use an overhaul, it is retro '60s, but what the heck, we're on vacation, and nothing beats running out by the ocean. If we go back to Punta Cana next year, I would definitely consider going back to the Riu.

<Content>Everything we hoped for! My wife and I recently stayed for two weeks at the Riu Taino, which we chose after comparing several resorts by their services and amenities, photos, and customer reviews. We were looking for a place where we could relax full-time, and where our most difficult decisions would involve nothing more stressful than whether to sleep in or get up early and watch the sunrise, whether to go swimming or have another pina colada, or whether to try the pasta or the grilled fish. For us the Taino turned out to be ideal.You'll find Riu Taino's services and accommodations listed in the travel sites, but here are some local observations.The unfavourable food reviews (which were often disappointingly vague), concerned us only until we arrived and sat down to our first meal. From that point on we ate happily and well. The selection and all-you-can-eat amplitude were certainly superior to what most people keep in their fridges and cupboards at home. One would be challenged to find a buffet anywhere capable of meeting everyone's tastes or dietary requirements, and perhaps the disgruntled reviewers are accustomed to either the very highest or the very lowest standards of cuisine. We were pleasantly satisfied with the high-end of in-between (a variety of choices both standard and unusual from among all the food-groups), and our only regret is that after two weeks we still hadn't managed to sample everything on offer. We strictly observed the warnings to not drink the tap water or even use it for tooth-brushing, and suffered no traveller's flu at all.The social atmosphere in the main building is relaxed; informal but not utterly casual. T-shirts and shorts are okay in the dining room except at dinnertime, when men are expected to wear long pants and shirts that cover the shoulders. Otherwise it's customary for guests (men and women alike) to spend their days half-naked. It is after all a hot country. Travellers to the Dominican Republic who speak only English should not expect absolutely fluent English in their hosts. That said, we had no communication problems when talking with the front-desk staff or with the travel representatives who maintain a desk nearby. The entertainment or animation staff around the pool and the beach spoke a limited but very enthusiastic mix of Spanish, English, French, and German. (German was by far the most common tongue we heard spoken among the guests.) The staff charged with table-service, room-cleaning, and grounds-keeping speak little or no English but are very good at their jobs. (The grounds-keepers let their machetes do the talking; they're particularly adroit at turning a fallen coconut into a drinking vessel in a matter of seconds.) We bought an inexpensive pocket-sized Langenscheidt Spanish-English dictionary at the small shop in the reception area, which was occasionally useful for making small-talk with some of the staff. Better still would be if we'd taken a few Spanish lessons in advance of our trip. Despite the language barrier we found the staff to be gracious, good-humoured and open, and wished that we could return their courtesy with more than a friendly nod and gesture.The weather and climate were phenomenal. Hot in the sun but perfect in the shade. A constant breeze blew day and night off the ocean, tempering the heat and humidity. In our room we relied on air-conditioning and a ceiling fan. But if you prefer to be struck senseless by tropical heat you have only to recline unsheltered on the beach or to sit on the private balcony adjoining your room. From there you can watch small lizards scurry among the lush abundance of palms and extravagantly-leaved plants (and, if you share my sensibilities, wish that you'd brought some nature books along for the trip). I was thrilled when a leaping tree-frog narrowly missed my head one evening as I was leaving our room. My wife was thrilled at the near-total absence of troublesome bugs. Neither of us felt ambitious enough to try snorkeling, much less scuba-diving, but we understand that there's much to be seen underwater just a few yards offshore. The surf breaks twice: first and most emphatically where it hits the shallows about two hundred yards out; then again, and more gently, where it finally rolls up onto the beach. These are manageable waves and good for adventurous children who might want to learn how to body-surf. In fact the resort is children-friendly and there were several families with young kids about. A word of caution though: the lifeguard stations on the beach were never occupied.Our room was bright and well-serviced but we were surprised to discover a double and a single bed within, not exactly what we had in mind for our belated honeymoon. We pushed the beds together and contented ourselves with that. The cleaning-staff seemed content as well and didn't correct our timid renovation for the duration of our stay, but the arrangement was awkward and we'd advise that you sort this sort of thing out with your agent or with the hotel beforehand if you want to spend some quality time nuzzling comfortably with your sweetheart after the sun goes down. If you need more inspiration you can tune into the porn channel on the TV, which begins broadcasting after 1:00 am or so. There are several local channels in Spanish and perhaps a half-dozen US channels including a sports network, a couple of movie networks, and a comedy network called 'CNN' that runs the same gag twenty-four hours a day: a perpetual spoof of televised news reportage.In theory you don't need your wallet once you've paid for your all-inclusive vacation and climbed aboard the plane. In practice you'll be expected to tip the bus driver who takes you from the airport to the resort, and you'll likely want to tip the porter who brings your bags to your room. To get that far you're best advised to shell out American dollars. Keep some small bills on hand to spare everyone the trouble of making change. From there on in everything's tip-free unless you feel otherwise inclined. But you can always find ways to spend money. The shops on Caribbean Street and the local flea-market vendors accept either US dollars or Dominican pesos. It's more fun to deal with the vendors, who are artfully just shy of aggressive and who don't mind to haggle. With a little pluck and some polite persistence you're bound to settle on a price you know you can afford, whether for jewellery, cigars, beach-wear or native art. Be aware that the Taino and its neighbouring Riu resorts offer no banking facilities. If you run out of cash you may have to hike eastward along the beach to the nearby Iberostar hotel, which has a bank that keeps somewhat murky hours. At the Iberostar at midday you can amuse yourself watching several pink flamingos pick their way through a tranquil pond while you wait for the bank clerk to return from lunch. You can bring whatever currency you like into the bank (traveller's cheques, credit cards, gold bullion - whatever) but you can convert it only into pesos. Also remember that you'll be required to pay a departure fee of $20 US (or the equivalent in pesos) per person before you board the plane for home.The only lowpoint of our vacation was self-inflicted and bears no reflection on the hotel services and staff. In our last-minute haste to pack for the trip we neglected to bring enough of the prescription drugs my wife requires daily for the treatment of a medical condition. These drugs were not available at the resort's small clinic or pharmacy, nor even at the nearest hospital several miles away. In the end we had to have the prescription sent by Fed-Ex from Toronto to Santo Domingo, the nation's capital and apparently Fed-Ex's only official Dominican destination. From Santo Domingo it had to travel by local courier to another city nearer to the resort, and from there it had to be forwarded by taxi. These complicated arrangements with various shippers outside the resort might have been impossible but for the extremely patient and generous help we received from Melvin, our Dominican Suntours/Alba representative, who spent hours on the phone interpreting on our behalf. We owe him an enormous debt of gratitude and hope that he never again has to deal with vacationers as reckless as ourselves. Don't leave home without your medication or anything else you absolutely need, and don't forget medical insurance.Apart from our own oversights we enjoyed a wonderful, restful, rejuvenating vacation. The weather was fantastic, the food and the swimming were excellent, and the staff were warmly accommodating. All in all the trip was great value for the money, and we wouldn't hesitate to return.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Feed the fishes!!!!! What a delight! For the past 12 months, I have been to Manzanillo, Cuba; Riu Jalisco in P. Vallarta and recently returned from Riu Taino at P.C. Comparing all 3, Riu Taino is the best trip so far. Check in: There's no wait. Eventhough there was about 10 of us, probably, the longest wait was 5 minutes. One evening we were relaxing at the lobby and noticed a bus of Germans coming in. Within less than 10 mins, everyone had their rooms and were gone. Room numbers are preassigned, and ready. Room: We sent an email earlier to request for specific rooms but found out later that they had not gotten the email. We were put at 741 which was quite a distance walking. Imagine the buildings (houses 4) are arranged in a grid formation away from the hotel. And if you happened to be at one of the last ones, it can get pretty far. Not sure if that's good or bad considering the amount of food you'll be eating! The exercise might do you good. However, we changed our rooms the next afternoon (at 1:00) and was given a better location (224). A/C in both the rooms worked well. No problems with water pressure, sink, nothing. Rooms are kept very clean. we tipped $2.00 a day. We got more than enough bottled water to gargle and brush our teeth, and drink since most of the time we're out of the room anyway. Honeymoon suite has a separate living quarter with a king size bed in the bedroom. Regular rooms are usually 1 double and 1 single. 3 pillows. I suggest if you're a picky sleeper like myself, bring your own feather pillow to sleep on. Occassionally we noticed a few ants here and there, and that's only because we left some of our sweet drinks on the nightstand. No big whoop.. small ants won't kill you. Clean, comfortable, good size for 2 person. Safe works and it's free so use it, of course common sense dictates that you don't leave your $100 watch in clear sight or your stash of cash lying around. Restaurants: Oh so many!! stay 1, play 4 is awesome. You can wonder off to the beach somewhere and when you're hungry, just drop by any restaurants (other than Palace) which is what we usually do (for lunch) Breakfast and dinner you have to be at your own restaurant. BUT, if you decide to go elsewhere for breakfast, no ones gonna know or stop you. There's no band on your hand except for palace. Breakfast has no preassigned seats either (dinner does). I recommend outside. It's cooler, nicer ambience. I liked the Melao's restaurants (outdoor is next to the main dining retaurant) for lunch. It's closer to the nicer part of Riu's beach, it's nothing fancy but food are pretty similar in all Riu's although if you're really picky about it, Bambu is slightly better than Taino is slightly better than Melao is slightly better than Naiboa. Over at Taino (next to Melao) there're 3 restaurants to choose from. The pizza house which is a pink building (but serves variety of food not only pizza), the main dining room and of course the outdoor restaurant. I noticed of all the restaurants, only the Pizza house serves seafood pealla (sp?) or chicken pealla. It's a form of rice cooked in seafood or chicken which is amazing. Go early, at 12, where it is hot. Sooo good. Sometimes, we took some paella and brought it over to the main dining. You can do anything you want. Lunch at Naiboa is average. Since not many ppl. there, food tend to be sitting for a while before it was replenished. Staff are friendly. I had zero problem with the food EXCEPT the soup is slightly too salty for me. Lots of variety to choose from. For ex. during dinner, there's ALWAYS chicken, beef, fish, pork, more fish, mussels, veal, cooked differently. Of course if you attempt to eat all of them everyday, naturally you would complain about why is the food always the same! And on top of that, they have carving stations, or hot pot stations (2 shirmp night, 1 curry night, 1 lobster night) Tues is Mexico night and Sat is DR night. Don't miss it. Be adventurous, try new things is my advice. If you're going to stick with your french fries and pan fried chicken breast then, it's really your loss. We tipped $2.00 each night for dinner. Service was good. We bought gifts (hats) for Aurelia at the pizza restaurant in Taino. One day, I was squeezing limes to make lemonade, she say me and insist I give her the peels and she threw it. Before I knew it, she was next to me again with a napkin. (this is before we even tip anything). Doesn't hurt to smile and be nice. One thing I was really shamed by fellow Canadians was this. During dinners, occassionally, they will be ppl. coming over to your table and serenade a song or two. All 3 couples did not bother to tip. I thought that was rude. I suggest if you have no money with you, at least say no thank you. If you don't tip the waiter or the room cleaning ladies, at least tip the singers. How rude!Beach: Excellent. Clear water on the first 3 days, semi clear on the remaining 3 days. Beach over at Melao and Taino are better than Bambu or Palace. Naiboa is not on the beachfront. Early morning we wake up and feed the fishes. Yes!! Grab a couple of buns or banana from the restaurants and feed the fish. Soooooo much fun. we saw about 7 or 8 kinds (3 with colors). As you walk out of Taino (watch out for the entertainment hall). Walk directly from the entertainment hall towards the beach and don't deviate. You'll come across some rocks (small part of beach is rocky) in the water. Go out to maybe shoulder height and enjoy! Best time is before 9 30 if you want to see colored ones. Sand is like butter on the beach. Pools: Naiboa! Good size, clean and quiet. If you want a quiet day by the pool, check out Naiboa. Shopping: They tell you that flea market is cheaper than Carribean street. Which is also a nice comfortable walk, about 10 mins from Taino. Bought a painting (about 3.5 feet by1.5 feet) for $45. Went to the my local print shop and he told me last night, it's a good quality oil painting. For that size, if you offer $20 (which we did initially) they'll say, go home! Now over at the carribean street it's about $90. We got some masks, some wooden figurines thingy as well. Carribean street is a host of shops in Riu compound. On Friday, it's street party. You have the Riu parade as well. Extremely chic tacky! very cool. Entertainment (animicion) Bambu has outdoors stage which I liked better. So most of the nights we went there. Entertainment wise, ... hey you can only do so much. Nothing special except one night where they had invited guest dancers and it was awesome. OTher than that, it was fun everynight. Lots of skits if you're into that. Flight/immigration: Skyservice now charges for their drinks as of Sept. 1. $1 for soda or bottle water. you want regular water, we can get it from the toilet tap if you like! and it comes with a big smile. If you've never been on skysevice, you should be aware that the seats are very tight. We had bistro style dinners and lunches. Meaning cold food - bread , salad, etc. Coffee and tea is free. No movies, TV broken it seems.Immigration and custom was a breeze. My passport is expired and was renewed. I left it on the expired page since that's where my picture is, and no problemo, didnt bother to check for the other pages for renewal :) Telephone: I don't know where's the number now, but there's a 1866 number to call the resort from North America to reach a guest. If the guests not in the room, no message, but feel free to call back later. Misc:Don't forget to pack yourself some food if you're gonna wait a while at the airport. a bottle of soda is $3, pringles, like $6... you get the idea. We bought mugs didnt even needed them since the bars are so close anywhere imaginable. Email me if you need more information

<Author>carlycunn
<Content>Just returned 6/18/03 - Great Time @ Taino My friend and I recently vacationed at Riu Taino, Dominican Republic. We had a fabulous time. She and I are single women (Ages 30 and 31). We booked our trip through Apple Vacations. We couldn't have been more pleased with the arrival and departure  the care the Apple representatives took to keep us informed during our stay. Our arrival was non-eventful, smooth. We had orginally booked our trip at Riu Naiboa but we were upgraded because the hotel was overbooked. When we arrived at Riu Taino, we had the pleasure of having Mejia at the reception desk be the person who checked us in. He was a joy! We requested a closer room to the beach the day we checked-in. Mejia arranged a new room for us the very next day. (Buidlings 27 and 28 are closest to the beach .. We were in room 343  it was a great location as well). Once we got settled into our new room, we were happy to find that he had sent us 2 bottles of rum and 2 souvenirs as well as a plate of delicious fruit to our new room. The pool and beach are beautiful. I went with hopes of getting a great tan. I'm happy to say I got it without much effort :-). The weather was great! It only rained one night at like 2am when I was fast asleep. We were there 8 days / 7nights. I was concerned about the weather because I had been monitoring the forecast on ... We learned after we got there that those forecasts primarily apply more to the inland than the coast. So, if you're watching the forecast and it says cloudy or rain, don't be too concerned. The forecast before we left said cloudy and showers every day. It was sunny every day with a few hours of overcast here and there. If your stay will include a Thursday night, you'll enjoy the activities on Carribean Street. The animation teams from each of the hotels bring the show to the street. Carribean Street is a nice touch to the resort. We also visited the vendors down the beach. I read alot of reviews saying that they are aggressive. I've been to Jamaica, St. Thomas, St. Maarten  found those vendors to be more aggressive. They are persistent but I walked right by many shops without any problem. If you're going to buy from the vendor (which I certainly did), be persistent  negotiate. When you ask how much, they will often ask how much you want to give .. start low no matter how ridiculous it seems. You'll be able to bargain better that way. Make sure you take smaller bills ($10, $5, $1) when visiting the vendors. My friend also went to Wal-Mart and purchased a few $5 wathces and used those as bargaining tools. It worked! We took the OUTBACK Safari tour  I highly recommend it. It's a great way to see the countryside, learn about the culture, and have fun at the same time. It's well worth the cost. The activity around the pool was fun. I didn't really do any of those activities until the day before we left. I was too busy on the beach :-) .. But, if you're there long enough try to get in some dance lessons, acqua gym .. The animation team is like everyone has said .. great! We did tip every now and then (i.e. tour driver, transfer driver from / to airport, baggage handler). We left small trinkets for the housekeeper daily (perfumed lotions, sprays, etc.). Our room was clean. The grounds are really a sight to see. There is one twin bed  one double bed. My friend and I alternated each night. Don't forget to pack wash clothes. There aren't any in the room. Now .. to the food .. which is always a concern. We didn't drink the tap water. I've gone to all inclusive resorts before. After a while, you can become bored with the buffet and the food.It's not an indication (to me) on the quality of food or service. It's just that after a while eating the same things over and over again become boring and dull. If my stay had been shorter, I may not have run into this problem. Breakfast was good. We packed Immodium and other things as preventative measure. I'm glad we had it because we needed it. I became sick on the fifth day of my stay. I stayed in the room all day  medicated myself - eating very little (Sprite and breads). I don't know that it was the food as much as it might have been my greediness .. (mixing all kinds of foods together). My friend also became sick. But, it wasn't enough to ruin or spoil our trip. We didn't let it dampen our enjoyment of Punta Cana. On a scale of one to five, I rate this resort a 4 - 4.5. I will eventually return. I had a splendid time!Don't let the bad reviews worry you. Most of the people we met and talked to there were quite pleased.Another thing to note -- Many of the reviews said that if you pay in American money, you'll get Peso in return/change. This is the case at the resort. However, outside the resort, we found that if we asked in advance if they'd give us US Dollar as change - we got it.It seems that families partiuclarly enjoyed the trip .. I saw lots of happy kids.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>All Inclusive is the way to go We stayed at Riu Taino from June 7-12. This was my first trip out of the country, so landing at this airport, which practically is just a grass hut, was awesome!!!! Our flight was delayed almost four hours from OHare, so we didn't even land until about 11:30 pm, which sucked, because it made it hard to see this beautiful island, and filling out those tourist cards in the dark was not the easiest task. When we arrived at Taino, it was completely dead, about 12:30am, so check in took about 30 seconds. I love how the lobby has no doors or windows, totally open. The thing I'll always remember is HOW CLEAN they keep everything. The grounds are amazingly spotless and every last bush and plant are pruned to perfection. They also keep the beaches very clean. Our first day there, we walked the beach to the orientation meeting (waste of time) and got lost on our way back. Everything looks the same from the beach!!! Every person we tried asking for directions back to Taino could not help us, as nobody speaks any English there. That is my only complaint, that they should know enough English to accompony vacationers. I was estatic to be topless on the beach, and didn't feel weird about it cause everyone else is doing it too. A lot of thongs too. The pool is absolutely amazing, very cool swim up bar. The all inclusive liquor made the trip, as I know I alone would have spent a few hundred dollars just in booze. The booze is different though, it's their own, no Absolute or Jack down there so don't even ask. It tasts different, but not bad. The OJ is more of a OJ/Mango mix. You room mini bar gets stocked every two days. The food is very good in the main dining room. But, if you want to keep it very casual, La Bamba bar/grill is pretty good too. They put green peppers in just about everything. People start to fill the pool area by 6-7 am, so if you want a lawn chair, get there early. I couldnt believe the amount of people in speedos and bikinis, who were very overweight. Humm, I'm sure they would have never wore that in their neighborhood. I love the little lizards running around everywhere! I love the African Masks I picked up there. There are some really nice treasures to be found there. Everyone I managed to talk to (very few) all said they had diarreah, and I didn't drink the water. I did drink a lot of booze though, all day long. I've been home 12 days and my stomach is still messed up somewhat. Willy and Abel at La Bamba were great, always remembered what I drank. Oh yeah, sand is everywhere, lol! I don't care how many times you shower, you still have sand on you, it's funny. Know how to count Pesos before you enter the store. Ladies, leave your make-up and blow dryers at home. It's too hot for make-up and you'll just sweat it off within 5 minutes and your hair, well lets just say 100% humidity. Just bring some gel and thats it. I could not find one shell on the beach, bummer. I hated to leave, as I love the tropics. The Punta Cana airport is a smoking airport, very cool. Not like OHare, where they want you there two hours before take off and they cant even give you one smoking room. I loved Punta Cana and would definately go back. Good value too. Our trip was only 583.00 per person for 5 days thru Apple vacations. You'll have a great time.

I travel a lot for work and I thought the rooms were great.I would definately go back to Punta Cana and if you are doing your research, I would strongly recommend the Riu Taino.

<Author>SXM03
<Content>Wonderful! After reading some of the reviews on this site, I was nervous for my 7 day trip to Riu Taino. I have to say, I don't know what they were talking about! We had a wonderful time!I am a very picky eater, and I thought the food was great. In fact, because I am so picky and I read that the food was so bad, I packed a ton of food and ended up bringing most everything home. Every meal has a buffet of every type of food imaginable. Every day for lunch and dinner there are french fries, rice, fresh fruit, pasta, and ice cream, among many other varied meats, vegetables, and desserts. There were theme nights where the menu and decorations followed the theme. I was also very worried about the water. There were three of us on the trip and none of us got sick. However we were very careful. You cannot drink the water, and some people say you can use it to brush your teeth, but don't! There is no need to risk it, there is a jug of purified water in your room, and I did hear one man say that he had diarrhea and he brushed his teeth in the water. The staff serves only bottled water at meals, and uses purified water to wash and cook all of the foods, as well as to make ice cubes. As long as you are careful, you'll be fine.The rooms were so clean! They change the sheets and wash the floor every day. The rooms have a fridge if you care to bring anything. There is always coke, diet coke, club soda, and alcohol in them. The rooms do not have a clock, so bring one! Also, bring a washcloth, they do not have them. The TV does have a porn channel, if you are bringing little kids you might want to be aware, rather than have them find it!Other random info: You get a towel card which you keep the whole time and exchange for a beach towel when you need it, we would get up, get a towel, put it on a chair by the pool, or on the beach, and then go eat breakfast. The area gets full (or at least the good areas with shade and sun) pretty quickly. We walked around to some of the other resorts, and in my opinion Taino wmuch older crowd and seemed too quiet. The staff was great. They had so much energy and were there to show you a great time. Tip: don't drink too much alcohol or caffeine during the day (without balancing it out with water) because that dehydrates you and gives you the same symptoms as if you drink the water. When we arrived, we had two rooms, and they were far away from each other, we asked to be moved closer and it was no problem. You may want to learn or write down some basic Spanish words though, the language barrier is tough. We went with Apple Tours; they were great, and extremely helpful. Overall, we had a wonderful relaxing time!!

<Content>Very Pleased Dear Travelers, We just returned from Riu Taino on March 17, 2003 after a 8 day trip. I just have to say that I found the Riu Resort to be excellent. Breakfast was to die for ...try the crossant french toast soooo good. Lunch was anywhere you wanted to go within the resort, they all had great things to choose from wether it was outside for causual burgers, hotdogs, or pizza and French Fries (or as we call them Freedom Fries) or inside for more detailed lunch items. Don't get me wrong...the food is different there is not alot of spices in it and the beef does taste different but it is good. We did not make any reservations for the specialty resturants for dinner we found out last year that you had more of a selection at the buffet.( Last year we went to Fiesta Bravaro ) Riu Taino was much nicer!As for the beaches ......JUST PARADISE relaxing in the sun or under the shade of the palm trees there is something for everyone. All in All I would recommend this resort to all ages. I can't believe anyone could have a bad time. I can't wait till I return.
